Agatha watched Sage make her way to their end of the table, a black Juul between her teeth like an unlit cigarette. She stopped next to Billy’s chair, tapped the back of it with her knuckles, and took the vape out of her mouth.

 

“Move,” Sage said.

 

Teen looked up, confused. “What?”

 

“You’re in my seat,” she said, nudging his elbow with her hip.

 

“There aren’t assigned seats,” he snapped, already turning back to Agatha. “Anyway- where were we?”

 

Sage didn’t give Agatha a chance to answer. Not that she could. She had no idea what he’d been rambling about before Sage walked over.

 

“You’ve been talking her ear off for twenty minutes,” Sage said. Then she kicked the leg of his chair. “You’ve had your turn. She looks miserable. Now get up.”

 

Billy turned to Agatha, offended. “We were having a great conversation,” he said, like he was speaking for both of them.

 

Agatha didn’t chime in. She took a sip from her drink and almost laughed.  She hadn’t minded the conversation, but watching them argue was a lot more fun.

 

“She hasn’t said a single word, dude.” Sage gestured to Agatha with both hands, presenting her evidence. “This isn’t a conversation, it’s a hostage situation.”

 

Agatha had to bite back another laugh, which came out as a snort. She covered her mouth with her hand, and when Billy whipped his head toward her, he looked slightly offended. That sure as shit didn’t stop him from doubling down.

 

“She’s a listener!” he said, talking for her again. “I know that because we’re friends. Plus, she doesn’t like you. She told me.”

 

Alright- friends was a stretch. A massive one, actually. And Agatha had said no such thing. But judging by the look Sage gave him, she already knew he was full of shit.

 

She looked at Agatha. “You tell him that?” Sage asked.

 

The way Sage was looking at her, she knew the girl wasn’t actually asking. Just making sure Billy had an audience when she called him out.

 

Agatha didn’t rush to respond. She looked at Sage for a beat, then said, “No.”

 

Sage looked back to Teen with a smile that was all teeth. “Would you look at that? That’s more than she’s said to you all night. So scram!”

 

Billy let out a long, dramatic sigh and stood up like he’d finally accepted he wasn’t winning. “Don’t forget we’re going to Eddie’s tomorrow,” he said, standing in front of Sage. “Bring your personality or whatever. I need all the help I can get.”

 

“I am not a vehicle for you to make out with my friend.”

 

Teen smiled at Sage and rested a hand on her shoulder, “You kind of are though.”

 

Then he turned and started toward the other end of the table. “Love you,” he called over his shoulder.

 

Sage sat down next to Agatha and grabbed a handful of popcorn like none of it had happened. After a second, she said, “You’re welcome.”

 

“Care to explain why the two of you are fighting for my attention tonight?” Agatha asked.

 

Sage shrugged. “Billy’s a try-hard and wants you to like him. Me? I just needed an excuse to get away from Amber throwing herself at Rio.”

 

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “That bad?”

 

“She called her mysterious. Twice. Then asked if she’d ever been in handcuffs. I had to get out before I lost my will to live.”

 

Agatha didn’t laugh, but her mouth twitched like it wanted to.

 

That sealed it. If she were ranking the overnight weekend x-ray shift, Sage had just taken the top spot without breaking a sweat.

 

-

 

Agatha wasn’t sure how they got here. Sage had pushed her chair back, legs stretched out, looking entirely too relaxed, while Agatha was sitting across from her tossing popcorn at her mouth with questionable aim.

 

They were asking each other questions now. Stupid ones. To pass the time.

 

“What’s the most embarrassing interaction you’ve had with a patient?” Agatha asked, tossing another piece of popcorn Sage’s way. It hit her shoulder and rolled off.

 

“I was sitting in the control booth,” Sage said. “Couldn’t see the guy our assistant brought in from the waiting room- he was in a wheelchair, behind the wall. So I ask, super casually, ‘Are you able to stand for your x-ray?’”

 

Agatha could already see where it was going.

 

“Silence. Like, dead silence. And then he says, ‘I don’t have legs.’”

 

Agatha snorted.

 

“I shot up like someone lit my ass on fire, looked through the window, and yep. No legs. I think I watched my soul exit my body and take the elevator to the morgue.”

 

Agatha lost it. Full laugh, head thrown back, snorting. She fired off another piece of popcorn mid laugh. Sage caught it in her mouth and threw her arms in the air like she’d just won a gold medal.

 

Agatha doubled over, still laughing. “That’s horrible.”

 

“Yeah, well,” Sage shrugged, still chewing, “it builds character.”

 

“Does it?”

 

“No,” Sage said, deadpan. “I wanted to fling myself off the roof of the hospital.”

 

Agatha shook her head, finally catching her breath as she tossed another piece of popcorn at Sage. She caught it again and let out a loud whoop. Then came the dance. All limbs and ego, loud enough to turn heads.

 

Agatha laughed under her breath and grabbed a whole fistful of popcorn, threw it up at her like confetti.

 

That’s when Agatha felt it.

 

She didn’t need to look to know. Her body already clocked it, same way it always did. Some internal barometer tilted whenever Rio looked at her, like a third eye rolling open, whispering: she’s looking at you.

 

When Agatha finally looked over, Rio was, of course, already staring at her. She didn’t smile or recoil or pretend to be looking somewhere else. The noise around them kept going. Alice kept talking. Sage was still dancing. Someone dragged a chair across the patio. None of it touched them.

 

Then Rio turned back to the group and let out a soft laugh at whatever Alice had just said. It came a moment too late, like she had to remember where she was.

 

Agatha shook it off and forced herself to laugh along with Sage, but it didn’t reach all the way.

 

Not seventeen minutes later, Rio stood up and walked over.

 

Agatha had been right. Same jeans. Same beat up Converse.  All that time, and Rio still moved through the world exactly the way Agatha remembered.

 

And for a second, that felt unfair.

 

“I’m gonna take Amber hom-”

 

“Thank god,” Sage said, cutting Rio off before she could finish.

 

Agatha snorted before she could stop herself. Tried to cover it with a cough, cleared her throat, and tossed out a half hearted, “Sorry,” in Rio’s direction without bothering to sell it.

 

Rio was looking at Agatha. Her brow was drawn, her mouth tugged upward, like she wasn’t entirely sure what had just happened or why she was reacting to it. It wasn’t quite a smile, not fully, but enough of one to be noticeable.

 

Rio moved her eyes back to Sage.

 

“You staying or ready for me to drop you off?”

 

Agatha hadn’t realized they came to game night together. Thinking back, Sage had spent most of the night near Rio before finally walking over and kicking Billy out of his own chair. Agatha had seen the two women leaving work together a few times too -crossing the parking lot, walking ahead of Agatha in the hall- but Agatha hadn’t given it much thought.

 

It wasn’t surprising. Agatha just hadn’t known they were that close. 

 

“Hard pass. I’ll hang out here,” Sage said immediately.

 

“Cool. I’ll be back in a few,” Rio said.

 

Rio moved to leave but slowed, eyes catching on the Jenga tower on the table. It had been sitting there untouched, half played, half forgotten. Her gaze flicked to Agatha, then back to the stack.

 

Rio reached for a piece.

 

Her fingers slipped around one of the lower corner blocks. It was the riskiest piece left, one someone didn’t touch unless they had something to prove. 

 

There had been a time when Rio would have passed it over without a thought, and wouldn’t care enough to try.

 

But not tonight.

 

Rio slid the block free. 

 

The tower wobbled under Rio’s touch, but it held.

 

Rio turned the piece over in her hand a few times, like she hadn’t decided what to do with it yet. For a second, Agatha thought she might set it down, walk away without placing it.

 

Then she looked at Agatha again.

 

And placed the block on top of the tower.

 

The tower didn’t collapse.

 

Rio didn’t say anything. She didn’t linger. She glanced once more at Agatha, then walked toward the backyard’s gate where Amber was calling her name.

 

Agatha didn’t ask what it meant. She just watched Rio go, knowing better than to pretend it hadn’t meant anything at all.

 

-

 

It was Agatha’s last shift of the week. She didn’t have a patient assignment all weekend. She was scheduled as the delivery nurse, which meant she had to stay ready in case a high risk birth came through. The delivery team was made up of people who could keep their heads when things turned sideways and Agatha, for better or worse, had a reputation for thriving in chaos.

 

If she was paged, she would head straight to the delivery room prepared to take over the moment a baby was born.

 

Until then, she floated. She stopped by different pods, leaned over shoulders, asked how things were going and actually meant it. If someone needed help with a feed or an IV or a baby who just wouldn’t settle, she stepped in without making a show of it. Sometimes she offered advice no one asked for. Sometimes she handed someone the thing they didn’t realize they needed until it was already in their hand.

 

Around 1:30 a.m., a trauma page came through: a pregnant woman, twenty-five weeks along, en route to the hospital. There was concern she might deliver before even making it upstairs to Labor and Delivery. Agatha was already moving.

 

She wasn’t alone. A whole team moved out at once- an NP, a resident, a fellow, a few NICU nurses, several from labor and delivery. They headed straight for one of the trauma bays in the ED. The patient was seventeen minutes out. Maybe less. Until then, they stood and waited.

 

Inside the room, things moved quickly. People were already calling out what needed to be ready -warmers, suction, respiratory, lines, someone call x-ray- even though Agatha had already spotted Rio leaning against the wall, arms crossed, waiting.

 

X-ray always was. 

 

Rio had mentioned it once, years ago. How x-ray always showed up first, stood there for twenty minutes while everyone else tripped over themselves to look useful, then got waved in like they hadn’t been there the whole time. At the time, Agatha had probably rolled her eyes. After that she saw it at every trauma she’d ever gone to.

 

Agatha hadn’t seen Rio since game night when she left with Amber and came back fifteen minutes later, alone.

 

Agatha pretended not to notice. Pretended the relief that hit wasn’t relief at all. Just digestion. Just ambient liquor. Anything but what it actually was. 

 

Though Agatha did the math- fifteen minutes wasn’t enough time to get very far, much less get away with anything. Whatever it was, it didn’t scream passion. It barely even whispered a poor decision.

 

They didn’t speak when Rio got back. But Agatha lingered a little closer than she had before. Close enough to watch Rio reshuffle a deck of cards with an unlit cigarette between her lips. Close enough to join the next round of blackjack, even though Agatha fucking hated blackjack.

 

Agatha lost on purpose… Maybe…  Hard to say.

 

She didn’t think about the Jenga tower.

 

Not the block Rio had pulled. Not the fact that it was one of the riskiest pieces- one Agatha never would’ve expected her to touch. Not the way Rio had hesitated, turning it over in her hand. And not the way she’d looked at Agatha just before placing it on top, like the act itself might carry more meaning than she was willing to give voice to.

 

Agatha could’ve obsessed over it. Could’ve dissected every second the way she used to when Rio was all questions and no answers, when every silence between them felt like a locked door she hadn’t been given the key to.

 

But she didn’t.

 

Agatha let it sit. 

 

A choice, a moment, a tower that didn’t fall.

 

Maybe it was Rio’s way of saying something. Or maybe it wasn’t. Maybe it was nothing at all.

 

Agatha didn’t need to know.

 

She didn’t want to keep reading into everything they did or didn’t do. She didn’t want their friendship to be a scavenger hunt for what might still be salvageable. She just missed Rio. Missed who they used to be when it didn’t feel like one wrong move would send everything crashing.

 

So Agatha told herself that not everything needed to be deciphered or had to mean more than it did.

 

Sometimes people just walked away.

 

Sometimes they came back.

 

Sometimes the tower held.

 

Agatha hadn’t realized she was standing still in the middle of the hallway until someone bumped her shoulder on the way past. The nurse aide muttered a quick “sorry” and slipped into the open trauma bay without looking back.

 

She blinked and the space around her came into focus again.

 

Rio hadn’t noticed her yet.

 

There was no assigned place to stand when a trauma was coming in. No rule about where she should be. The trauma bays stretched out on either side of the hallway, curtains drawn back and waiting. Plenty of places to choose from and stay out of Rio’s way.

 

But Agatha didn’t want them to keep dodging each other like this. Didn’t want group nights to feel like a custody arrangement. Didn’t want to keep pretending that closeness had to come with consequence.

 

So Agatha crossed the hallway and made her way to the portable. 

 

She leaned against the portable without looking at Rio, hands tucked into her pockets.

 

Out of the corner of her eye, she saw Rio shift. Saw the slight turn of her head, the tightening of her jaw like she was half a second away from snapping at whoever thought the x-ray equipment doubled as furniture.

 

Rio saw who it was and said nothing.

 

“Can someone call x-ray?” someone shouted from inside the bay.

 

“They’re already here,” Agatha called back, flat and loud, not bothering to hide the irritation in her voice. Agatha rolled her eyes. It was amazing how people could walk past a machine the size of a chest freezer and still act like it was invisible.

 

After a breath, she let herself glance sideways.

 

Rio was already looking at her, the corners of her mouth pulling upward,  trying not to smile.

 

Agatha turned her head away, eyes forward again, but she felt it. That tug of a smile she didn’t bother fighting all the way down.

 

Agatha let it sit. 

 

A choice, a moment, a tower that didn’t fall.

 

-

 

Agatha was walking out of the building when her phone buzzed in her pocket. She pulled it out, thumbed open her messages, and immediately rolled her eyes.

 

Alice had created a group chat. She called it Coven of Chaos. Everyone was in it.

 

Alice: 70s night at The Witches Road on Wednesday. Be there or end up in B Squared.

 

Agatha snorted under her breath. Stupid joke.

 

B Squared was what the ED staff called the psych hallway- technically part of B Pod, but set off in its own little corridor in the middle of the department, shaped like a square.

 

She didn’t bother replying. Just started to tuck her phone away when another text came through.

 

This one was from Rio.

 

Her name lit up the screen like it had never left. Agatha had changed phones at least three times in the last decade, but Rio’s number had always made the jump. She’d never deleted it. Had never even hovered over the option.

 

The text was three emojis: A knife and two drops of blood.

 

Agatha stared at it for a second, then opened a separate thread. Just the two of them.

 

It was empty. A blank conversation. No record of what came before. A fresh start, if Agatha wanted to believe in that kind of thing.

 

She typed quickly and didn’t overthink the words.

 

Next time wear a neon sign or something.

 

There was no explanation attached. She didn’t need one. Rio would know exactly what she meant. The trauma bay. The shouting. The way the entire team acted like x-ray hadn’t been standing there the whole time.

 

Agatha slid her phone into her pocket and kept walking.

 

-

 

Agatha didn’t check her phone until the alarm blared at noon.

 

After her third and final night shift of the week, the routine was always the same- go home, crash until noon, then force herself to stay up until at least nine. It was the only way to reset her schedule without spiraling into a four day blackout. Miserable, but necessary. If she didn’t do it, the alternative was she’d sleep through the next four days and wake up just in time to go back to work.

 

Agatha groaned, rubbed at her eyes, already irritated before she was fully conscious. The alarm was too loud, and she was mad at it for doing exactly what she told it to do. She slapped at her nightstand until her fingers found the screen, then tapped it into silence.

 

After a long breath, she pushed the blankets off and swung her legs out of bed with another groan. She grabbed her phone without looking at it and trudged downstairs, fully prepared to start the day by resenting every second of it.

 

In the kitchen, she leaned against the counter while the Keurig sputtered to life. The scent hit before the cup was halfway full- burnt, cheap, slightly metallic, like comfort wearing the wrong clothes. She didn’t even like it. But it was what she drank.

 

She unlocked her phone and scanned the notifications.

 

One missed spam call. A dozen new texts from the group chat. Two that weren’t.

 

Wanda and Rio.

 

Agatha immediately opened the group chat first.

 

Most of it was chaos- people confirming they’d be at 70s night, half finished inside jokes, photos from the last game night. Agatha scrolled, not expecting to care, until her thumb paused on a picture.

 

It was her and Sage.

 

Sage was mid victory dance, arms thrown up in a blur, popcorn suspended in the air around her like confetti. Agatha was laughing- head tilted back, eyes shut, mouth open in a way that made it clear she hadn’t seen the camera and wouldn’t have cared if she had.

 

She looked happier in that photo than she had in a long time. Happier than any picture from Chicago.

 

She saved the picture without thinking.

 

The next photo was from blackjack. Jen must’ve taken it too. Agatha was staring down at her hand, fully focused, bottom lip caught lightly between her teeth. Beside her, Teen was mid eye roll, his chips stacked unevenly. Alice sat next to him mid reach, stealing chips from Teen’s stack. Sage was grinning at the end of the table, one foot on the ground with the other propped on the edge of the table, her cards already tossed. And Rio was in the corner of the frame, legs tucked to her chest, cards already down, both middle fingers lifted toward the camera.

 

Agatha had spent years trying to replicate this photo- dinners in Chicago, couples’ trips, birthdays. The pictures always looked fine. Beautiful, even. But her posture told the truth. Just a little too careful. A little too aware of where the camera was.

 

But here, Agatha wasn’t even smiling. She wasn’t performing. She was just in it.

 

And somehow, that looked closer to joy than anything she’d ever been able to fake.

 

Agatha saved that photo too.

 

As she scrolled, she saw someone had replied directly to the photo of her and Sage.

 

xxx-xxx-xxxx: billy i hope this pisses you off so bad.

 

Sage. 

 

Agatha saved her contact information, and scrolled further.

 

Teen: i’m not jealous i just think it’s suspicious how sage only experiences joy when she’s stealing emotionally significant bonding moments between me and agatha.

 

Teen: fine. IT SHOULD’VE BEEN ME

 

Agatha rolled her eyes, swiped out of the group chat, and opened Wanda’s message first. Bad news before the good, she reasoned.

 

Wanda M.: I miss you. Call me later?

 

“Yuck,” Agatha whispered, staring at Wanda’s message. She grabbed her coffee from where it had just finished brewing on the Keurig and took a sip, hoping it would scald the bad taste left in her mouth from her ex-wife’s text.

 

Agatha had a hunch that game night had already made its way to Instagram. Or Facebook. Or whatever Wanda platform still scrolled like her morning newspaper.

 

Wanda was chronically online in the worst way. Every meal, every milestone, every moment worth bragging about ended up posted. Agatha couldn’t count the number of times she’d been forced to smile for pictures she hadn’t wanted to take, standing in front of things she hadn’t wanted to see.

 

She opened her own Facebook app. It hadn’t been touched in years and looked it. Outdated profile picture. A graveyard of old comments she didn’t care to ever look at. She typed in Jen’s name and hit search.

 

Jen had posted three photos. One of her and Agatha. The popcorn moment with Sage. And a full group picture that happened to include Rio being annoyingly photogenic.  All under a caption so nauseating it should’ve come with a warning label.

 

The One Where The Covenless Witch Returns To Her Coven.

 

We missed you!!!

 

It was the gayest fucking thing Agatha had ever read.

 

That was all Agatha needed to confirm what she already suspected- Wanda had seen the post. She always saw posts like that. 

 

Kale could’ve posted a blurry picture of Agatha’s elbow and Wanda still would’ve found it within minutes.

 

Agatha didn’t know what Wanda wanted and didn’t care enough to wonder. Maybe it was jealousy. Maybe guilt. Maybe some twisted attempt to reassert control now that Agatha was- what? Laughing in public? Being in Rio’s general vicinity?

 

More likely, Wanda had just assumed Agatha would be miserable without her.  Westview never fit into Wanda’s plan. Neither did anything resembling hapiness. And certainly not Rio Vidal.

 

When the divorce came up, they spoke mostly in terms of logistics. Wanda suggested Agatha should stay in Chicago. Claimed she seemed happier there.

 

Happier doing what, exactly?

 

Chicago had offered distraction. Polite conversations, a calendar full of shit that didn’t matter, and enough self restraint to keep from screaming in public.

 

Agatha only knew two things for sure: Wanda despised Westview.

 

And Wanda never once tolerated Rio Vidal.

 

It didn’t take a rocket scientist to figure out why her ex-wife was suddenly reaching out.

 

Agatha hadn’t spoken to her since that phone call where Wanda agreed too easily at the idea of them sleeping together again, then pretended to forget the name of the only person she’d ever truly resented.

 

"I MiSs YoU. CalL mE lAtEr," Agatha mocked, flatly, to no one.

 

That wasn’t to check in.

 

Agatha didn’t reply to Wanda’s text. She wasn’t going to. Empty sentiment didn’t warrant a response.

 

She hadn’t opened the app in years, hadn’t posted, liked, or reacted to anything. Her profile was a digital ghost town. But if there was even the slightest chance Wanda would see Agatha’s name pop up publicly -proof that Agatha was alive, present, and having a better time than she was supposed to- then yes. Agatha would log in. She would scroll. And she would leave a comment.

 

Agatha’s thumbs hovered for a second, then typed the comment.

 

Happy to be home <3

 

Her name floated to the top of the post, right where it needed to be.

 

She slid out of the app, slid down her home screen, and tapped the notifications from Rio.

 

Rio: tried that. didn’t work.


Rio: was thinking a flare gun next time. maybe they’d notice that.

 

Agatha read it once, then again. And despite everything, she laughed.

 

She didn’t even get a chance to think of a response before Wanda’s contact picture covered her entire screen.

 

Calling Agatha. Not even five minutes after she commented on Jen’s post.

 

Agatha let out a groan, took a long sip of coffee, and stared at the phone while it rang. She made no move to answer. When it finally stopped, she set the mug down and finished responding to Rio.

 

Unfortunately, that was funny.

 

Another text pinged in immediately after- Wanda again.

 

Because of course it was.

 

Wanda M.: I saw the post. You look good. Really. Just wanted to hear your voice.

 

Agatha locked her phone. Set it face down on the counter.

 

Then it pinged.

 

Once.

 

She stared at it for a second. Didn’t move. Didn’t care.

 

Then she turned it over.

 

Rio: unfortunately… i’m funny.

 

Agatha stared at it, jaw tight, already annoyed with herself for grinning.

 

She locked the screen again.

 

Unlocked it thirty seconds later.

 

Let’s not get ahead of ourselves.

 

She hit send and, without thinking, called Jen.

 

It rang twice.

 

“Harkness,” Jen said, voice flat.

 

“Kale.”

 

A pause.

 

“What now?”

 

Agatha pressed her elbows into the counter and dragged a hand over her face. “Apparently being visible online is a formal invitation for harassment-”

 

Her phone buzzed against her ear. She pulled it away to glance at the notification banner at the top of the screen.

 

Wanda… Again.

 

Agatha groaned, then brought the phone back to her ear.

 

“She’s blowing up my fucking phone, Jennifer.”

 

Jen didn’t pause before answering. “That’s not new. She pulled the same shit a decade ago.”

 

“Did she?” Agatha asked.

 

Lie.

 

A big, fat, obvious lie.

 

Jen snorted. “Don’t bullshit me now, Harkness. You remember exactly what happened. If she so much as heard Rio might be somewhere near you, she’d blow up your phone until you came home.”

 

Agatha pressed her lips together. She remembered. Of course she did.

 

“I think that’s a bit of an exaggeration.”

 

She didn’t know why she said it. Maybe to cover the fact that she'd treated a parade of red flags like they were love letters.

 

“Agatha. She hated Rio.”

 

“No, it wasn’t-”

 

“She said, and I quote, ‘That woman is an evil Skeletor and a very gross person to be around.’”

 

Silence.

 

“Okay.” Agatha said, already smiling. “Not that I’m defending that, but she’d just watched Rio eat a hot wing, panic, snort milk through her nose, and watched said milk flow out of her mouth and into the kitchen sink.” Agatha paused and sighed, before quickly saying, “It was horrifying and I still think about it… Fondly.”

 

“That’s because it was fucking hilarious,” Jen said, in full defense. “And your ex was.. is....whatever... the biggest buzzkill I’ve ever met.”

 

Agatha scoffed, “Okay, well. It’s not like anyone told me not to marry her.”

 

Jen didn’t say anything right away. When she did, her voice was quieter. “We tried,” she said. “You just didn’t want to hear it unless it came from her.”

 

Rio.

 

Agatha hummed and took a sharp inhale, narrowed her eyes at the toaster, “Jennifer…” she sang in a warning lullaby. “Keep talking like that and you’re gonna lose privileges.”

 

“Agatha,” Jen said, mocking her song exactly. “The fact I haven’t yet after that last comment already says more than you think.”

 

Agatha didn’t argue. She didn’t even deflect.

 

Jen exhaled, “Wow. So that’s still a thing.”

 

Agatha rubbed at her forehead, eyes shut tight. “Maybe,” she muttered quietly. 

 

And that was the closest she’d come to telling the truth.

 

“You still in denial?” Jen asked, tone lighter than the question deserved.

 

“I’m in denial about a lot of things.”

 

Jen didn’t push. Just pivoted.

 

“Well… you could come over. I’ve got wine and you have terrible dating apps. We can judge strangers until it feels like therapy.”

 

“It’s one in the afternoon,” Agatha said flatly.

 

“And?”

 

Agatha sighed. “I’ll be there in twenty.”

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

They weren’t even through their second glass of wine, and Agatha was already buzzed enough to stop pretending she had any standards. Their wine glasses had been abandoned on the coffee table entirely forgotten. Agatha and Jen sat shoulder to shoulder, thumbs ruthless. They’d made it through seven strangers on Bumble. Their commentary vicious and their judgment was swift. 

 

Jen suddenly gasped.

 

Loud. Dramatic. Enough to make Agatha’s stomach drop.

 

Of course. Of course.

 

Rio fucking Vidal.

 

Typically this was the part where Agatha would hurl her phone into the nearest trash can, or ideally, into another universe, before her rage even had a chance to finish blooming. But there was no rage this time. She didn’t know what she felt. Only that she couldn’t look away from her phone screen.

 

Rio was staring straight into the camera, head tilted, cheek pressed to her hand. Her elbow rested on a white cube- table? Box? -something intentionally abstract, like it had been staged by someone who understood angles. The lighting was perfect. Too perfect.

 

Her hair was messily arranged and it screamed effort disguised as accident. A thin gold chain traced the line of her collarbone. She wore black. Thin straps. Low neckline. Could’ve been a dress, could’ve been a tank top, and Agatha hated that she couldn’t tell. She wanted to know. She needed to know how much of Rio’s skin was just out of frame.

 

Rio looked fucking devastating.

 

Unreasonably so.

 

Like the photo had been engineered specifically to ruin Agatha Harkness.

 

“Who took that?” was all Agatha could manage, barely above a whisper.

 

Jen hesitated. “Me?” It came out more like a question than a confession.

 

Agatha turned her head slowly, narrowing her eyes. Jen looked suddenly very interested in the ceiling.

 

“So,” Agatha said, licking her lips, drawing the pause out like she wasn’t trying at all. “Was she, uh... in a dress? Or was it, like, a tank top and jeans situation?” She even shrugged, casual as hell.

 

The most casual question in the world… By Agatha’s standards, anyway.

 

“I don’t see why that matters-”

 

“No,” Agatha cut in, too fast. She cleared her throat and tried again, softer this time. “No. It doesn’t. I just... wanted to know. And since you were there, I think you should let me know.”

 

Agatha reached for her phone, still in Jen’s hand.

 

Jen pulled it just out of reach. “Agatha.” Her tone dropped. A warning.

 

Agatha tilted her head, eyebrows raised in perfect innocence. “What?”

 

Jen didn’t buy it. “What are you going to do?” she asked, slowly, carefully, like she already regretted handing over her wine.

 

Agatha glanced at the screen again then shifted her gaze to the traitor sitting beside her. She sucked her teeth, loud enough to make Jen flinch.

 

“Nothing,” Agatha said, reaching out. “Just give me my phone back.”

 

“No.” Jen yanked it farther away.

 

Agatha let out a breathy laugh, all disbelief. “Jen. Be serious. Give me my phone.”

 

“I am being serious. You’re making that face you make before you do something that requires damage control.”

 

“I’m not-” Agatha stopped herself. Then, grinning wide, too wide -more wolf than woman- she tilted her head. “Tank top or dress?”

 

“That’s not helping your case,” Jen hissed.

 

Alright. Fuck it.

 

“Give me the phone, Jen!” Agatha shouted and launched.

 

“NO!” Jen shrieked, halfway to scrambling off the couch when Agatha tackled her. They crashed to the floor in a tangle of limbs and shrieking laughter and very real threats.

 

“Agatha!” Jen gasped, utterly betrayed, halfway pinned.

 

“Give me my fucking phone!” Agatha growled through clenched teeth, wrestling.

 

“No! This is why I don’t invite you over for wine anymore!” Jen shouted, twisting as Agatha climbed over her. “You get horny and scary and you make terrible decisions!”

 

“You literally gave me the wine!” Agatha shouted back, lunging again.

 

“I was trying to be nice!” Jen screeched.

 

In the mess of limbs and shouting, Agatha somehow managed to knock her phone loose. It slid across the floor out of Jen’s reach. She threw her weight forward, pinning Jen down with her knees bracketing her sides. She grabbed two fistfuls of Jen’s shirt and shook.

 

“TANK TOP OR DRESS?”

 

Jen’s eyes went wide, arms flailing uselessly. “Dress! It was a dress! Jesus, get off me!”

 

Agatha instantly loosened her grip, all menace evaporating into smug satisfaction. “Huh?” she breathed. “See? That wasn’t so hard, was it, Jenny?”

 

She leaned in and planted a loud, obnoxiously wet kiss on Jen’s cheek then scrambled off her, making a break for her phone.

 

Jen grabbed for her legs. She almost got Agatha.

 

Almost.

 

Agatha went down hard -elbows first, a short, ugly fall- but didn’t let it stop her. She hit the floor and kept moving, crawling the last few feet because she was a woman on a mission. Her fingers closed around the phone, flipped it over, screen up. She swiped right on Rio’s profile without a moment of hesitation.

 

A cheerful chime sounded.

 

YOU MATCHED! lit up the top of the screen in big, celebratory letters.

 

Agatha’s breath came in short, uneven bursts, her grin stretched wide and wild as she shoved the phone inches from Jen’s face. “A-ha! Look at that- it’s a match!”

 

Jen didn’t even flinch. “Okay? And?” she snapped, swatting the phone away. “You literally said you just wanted to be friends with her when you got here. Only friends, Agatha. How is this helping that?”

 

Okay, so maybe Agatha had said that.

 

Maybe, when she first got there, wine still uncorked and self control fully intact, she did tell Jen she wanted to try being friends with Rio again. That was all. And if anything was going to happen between them, it would only be friendship.

 

Completely standard. Deeply adult. Uncomplicated platonic friendship.

 

Agatha just... hadn’t expected to see her face. Not like that. Not staring into the camera like she'd been waiting for Agatha to find her. Like the whole profile had been made just to get under her skin. Which, obviously, it hadn’t. Obviously . 

 

Which was so much worse. Because it wasn’t bait. It wasn’t a challenge. It was just Rio on a stupid fucking dating app.

 

And Agatha wasn’t above taking that personally.

 

“Yeah, well… friends can match! It’s fine. It’s friendly matching.”

 

And there it was again- the Nile, in all its slow, inevitable glory. Still Agatha’s favorite vacation spot, apparently.

 

In Agatha’s defense -because someone had to defend her, and it sure as hell wasn’t going to be Jen- she had also mentioned, on the phone earlier, that she was in denial about a lot of things. That wasn’t a secret. It was a disclaimer. A legal warning, if you will.

 

“Oh my god, Agatha,” Jen said, flat on her back, staring up at her in disbelief.

 

“What?” Agatha snapped. “I’m not going to message her. I just needed to know if she swiped right. That’s all. It’s perfectly reasonable.”

 

Jen looked unconvinced.

 

Agatha kept going. “And she did. So now I know. It’s not weird. It’s not anything. It’s just... confirmation.”

 

“Confirmation,” Jen repeated, deadpan.

 

“That we can be friends,” Agatha clarified.

 

Jen gawked at her. “So let me get this right. You needed to match with your ex-... not-ex… almost… whatever the fuck that situation is- to confirm that being just friends is on the table?”

 

“Bingo, Jennifer.” Agatha pointed at Jen, triumphant. “See? You’re catching on.”

 

“That doesn’t make any sense!” Jen snapped, her arms flailing like she was trying to physically beat Agatha’s logic out of the air.

 

“It does if you’re a student of platonic dynamics.” Agatha fired back, dead serious.

 

“What the hell happened?”

 

Agatha turned fast. Alice stood in the entryway, wide eyed and frozen. Jen was already sitting up beside her, rubbing her ribs, blinking at the mess like she wasn’t entirely sure how they got there.

 

But Agatha barely registered either of them. Just sat there, wild haired and wide eyed, trying not to betray the very obvious fact that she had completely lost control of the situation.

 

Because standing just behind Alice was Rio.

 

Agatha’s stomach dropped. Her mind blanked. Her heart was now sitting firmly in her ass. All the air she thought she’d been breathing was ripped from her lungs on sight.

 

And then Agatha’s brain started defending itself.

 

She hadn’t swiped because she cared. Obviously. She swiped because she was curious. And curiosity didn’t mean interest, it meant stability. That she could look the past in the eye and walk away from it. She just needed to know if Rio had swiped too. That was it. Nothing dramatic. Nothing romantic. Just proof they were both adults. That the door was shut. That it had always been shut. That they were... whatever.

 

Fine. Friends. Colleagues.

 

And if Rio had swiped first? That meant she was the one hanging on, not Agatha. If it was mutual, then it didn’t count. It canceled itself out. It proved the opposite of what it looked like. It was math.

 

So, no- Agatha didn’t regret it. She was gathering evidence. Scientific. Reasonable. Completely detached.

 

Until said evidence showed up in the doorway.

 

Now the living room looked like a crime scene. Jen was holding her side. Alice was still blinking at the mess. Wine pooled beneath the table. Agatha hadn’t even realized her sweatshirt had slipped halfway off her shoulder. She looked feral.

 

And Rio was just standing there. Quiet. Watching.

 

She scanned Rio instinctively. No phone in hand. No screen. No proof she’d seen it.

 

Good. Small miracles.

 

“Agnes is what happened,” Jen announced, far too pleased with herself.

 

Agatha jabbed a finger in her direction. “I told you to stop calling me that.”

 

Agnes O’Conor. 

 

Agatha had nothing kind to say about her. She hated that woman with a fucking passion.

 

Fourteen years ago, after several regrettable glasses of boxed wine, Jen, Alice, and Rio had named the monster that crawled out when Agatha tipped past her third glass.

 

Jen wasn’t wrong, though. Wine, any kind of wine, turned Agatha into a terrifying, unhinged gremlin of a person. Horny, reckless, emotionally dangerous. Agnes had no filter, no self preservation instinct, and an alarming tendency to drag Agatha’s worst secrets into the light just to watch them burn.

 

Yeah. Agnes had made an appearance today. But right now, Agatha was painfully sober.

 

Agatha looked back at Rio, who had tucked her hands into the back pockets of her jeans and was rocking absently on the balls of her feet. Her lips were pulled into her mouth, either to hide a grin or to trap whatever stupid question she was dying to ask that would absolutely, without fail, piss Agatha off.

 

Possibly both.

 

Alice let out a low whistle. “Hurricane Agnes makes landfall.”

 

Agatha didn’t look away from Rio. “Don’t,” she warned, already seeing the gears turning behind Rio’s eyes. “Whatever you’re about to say, swallow it. Along with your pride, your smugness, and preferably yourself.”

 

Rio raised her hands in mock surrender, lips twitching but silent.

 

That counted as a win.

 

So of course Rio had to ruin it by stepping back, stretching her arms overhead like she had nowhere better to be, and casually announced, “I, uh… I think I’m gonna step out for a smoke.”

 

The second the door clicked, Agatha shot to her feet. “Are you fucking kidding me, Alice?”

 

Alice shrugged. “What? The Liberty play at four.”

 

Agatha didn’t answer. She followed Rio out the door before she could think better of it.

 

“Sweet. Nothing I love more than scrubbing Merlot out of a rug!” Jen called out after her.

 

Agatha had no plan. She didn’t know what she came out here to do. Damage control? Maybe. That would’ve required forethought, which wasn’t exactly her strong suit today.

 

She turned the corner of the house and there was Rio. Leaning against the brick, one foot kicked up behind her, cigarette burning steady between her fingers. Both hands held her phone too close to her face. Her expression was still, it meant she was reading something twice to make sure it was real.

 

Agatha didn’t need to ask what it was. She already knew.

 

Somehow, this felt worse than if Rio had been laughing.

 

Agatha cleared her throat.

 

Rio startled, just barely but it was there. She stuck the cigarette between her lips and she fumbled with her phone, shoving it into her back pocket with all the grace of someone pretending it hadn’t been the most interesting thing in the world thirty seconds ago.

 

She took a slow drag from her cigarette, eyes forward now, like Agatha hadn’t just caught her seeing exactly what she came out here to deny.

 

Agatha didn’t call her on it.

 

She walked up instead and nodded toward the cigarette between Rio’s fingers. “Can I bum one?”

 

Rio eyed her for a second, then pulled the pack from her pocket and tapped one loose without a word. She passed it over, cigarette still balanced between her own lips, eyes already moving somewhere else as she shoved the pack away again.

 

“Thought you were too good for Spirits now?” Rio muttered around the cigarette, then reached up and pulled it free.

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “A light?”

 

Rio paused.

It was small. Purple metal. Still carried that soft shine underneath the years of being carried, dropped, and used. And on the side, scratched faint but permanent: A.H.

It would be in the sleeves Agatha would borrow, in the collar she’d adjust without meaning to, in the room long after Rio had gone.

Stupid question .

Platonic .

 

That word still had teeth. All these years later, it could still sink in, still tear at the places she thought had hardened over.

 

That was what they had always been. Perfectly platonic, painfully careful. Two cowards orbiting the same fire, pretending they couldn’t feel the heat. They’d become experts at it because it was easier than wrecking the only thing they had ever gotten right.

 

And still, even playing it safe, they found a way to lose each other.

 

“I mean it,” Agatha snapped. “No weirdness. No… tension. None of the old bullshit.”

 

Rio tilted her head, studying her. “You want to be friends again?” She said slowly. 

 

Agatha’s jaw tightened.

 

Friends were safe. Friends were manageable.

 

Agatha held Rio’s gaze, refusing to flinch. “I want you back in my life.”

 

“Friends, then.” Rio’s mouth pulled into a wide grin, flashing that familiar gap between her teeth. Agatha ignored the way her chest tightened at the sight.

Sinner, you better get ready.

Rio: are you coming to The Road for 70s night

 

Agatha stared at the text. Jen and Alice had been quite annoying about it the last few days. Said the bar missed her. Said it wasn’t the same without her. And clearly it had worked, because she was currently standing in her bathroom, getting ready anyway.

 

Theme nights used to be her thing. She crushed them, every time- costumes, energy, all of it. Of course, it was never Wanda’s scene. Her ex-wife liked velvet ropes and overpriced cocktails and any place that had a dress code longer than the menu. Agatha used to pretend she didn’t miss the dive bars and the chaos that came with it. Agatha wasn’t in Chicago anymore. She didn’t have to pretend.

 

Agatha typed out a quick reply.

 

Maybe. 

 

She and Rio had been doing the friend thing for a whole two days now, which mostly meant not making it weird. After their talk on Monday, Rio had asked if she wanted to stick around and watch the basketball game with her and Alice and Jen. Agatha said yes. It went… well. They kept to opposite corners of the couch, traded jokes, let it be easy. It was nice. It was normal.

She shoved her phone aside, screen down, and leaned back toward the mirror to finish her makeup.

Her sleeveless blazer hung open down the front, nothing underneath, the gold embroidery glinting every time the lights spun overhead. Her gold sequined pants caught the glow of the disco ball, flashing with every step. Fingerless mesh gloves and a decorated headband tied around her forehead finished her look.

Some things never change.

“Thanks,” she said, giving him a quick once-over. He was drowning in a massive, fluffy blue jacket that looked like it belonged on a parade float. “You look… warm.”

“Want to start a tab?” he asked, already reaching for the register.

 

“Put it on mine, Max!” An unfamiliar voice came from somewhere to Agatha’s left.

 

Max gave a quick nod and moved down the bar.

“Nah,” the woman said, smiling back at her. “Rebecca dragged me out. I’m a sucker for a good theme night.”

The woman laughed and shifted closer, casual enough to pass for friendly if anyone was watching but not subtle enough to miss.

 

“Making new friends without me?”

It stole the breath from Agatha’s lungs and left her stomach lurching in a way that felt both familiar and entirely new.

 

Before Agatha could open her mouth to respond, Rio reached out and wrapped her fingers loosely around her wrist, tugging Agatha gently.

 

“Come on,” Rio said, her voice easy. “You’re wasting your time down here. Drinks are better at the other end.”

For a moment, Agatha wasn’t sure who she had walked away from, only that she hadn’t hesitated.

 

It was pathetic, really- how easily she left. How little it took. No resistance, no second thought. Just a hand at Agatha’s wrist and whatever instinct that lived in her bones, telling her to follow Rio.

 

Agatha turned forward again and kept walking. And as she walked, she swallowed the humiliating truth that it would have taken just as little ten years ago.

 

The noise of the bar washed over them, people shifting around them, and Agatha let it, let it distract her from the fact that nothing about this felt normal, not even close.

 

They were halfway to the other end when she felt Rio’s hand sliding down from her wrist, slipping into her palm, and tangling their fingers.

 

Agatha blinked once, kept walking, kept pretending she understood what was happening even though every part of her brain was stuck on the feeling of their hands linked together.

“Another whiskey, neat,” Rio said, then added, “and a Dos Equis.”

 

Agatha laughed because- seriously, what the fuck just happened?

 

The bartender looked up. “You want it dressed?”

 

He didn’t ask about the drink Agatha had left behind at the other end, still sweating on the bar having been abandoned mid conversation.

 

“Yes- wait. No. No I- just no.” The words came tumbling out of Rio's mouth.

 

The bartender nodded and turned away.

 

Agatha said nothing, but her eyes flicked toward Rio. 

 

She knew what that had been. A half step forward. A reach. An attempt. 

 

No matter what, Rio never ordered her beers dressed. She actually preferred it that way, but Rio hated how the salt and lime juice made the bottle sticky, which made her hands sticky, which meant the salt stuck to her lips. It was a whole chain reaction she refused to deal with.

 

So Rio avoided it. Every time.

 

It wasn’t about preference. It was about control. Quiet, specific, and impossible not to notice once you knew her.

She didn’t think about how Rio had clearly been trying to prove something again, or how pissed off and embarrassed Rio looked at herself when she couldn’t follow through.

She wasn’t.

 

Rio’s touch was enough to be dismissed as incidental, but also lingered long enough to ask.

 

This was fine. Completely fine. Friends held hands. That was normal. Probably even healthy. Certainly more normal than being cockblocked by said friend in a bar. This, at least, had plausible deniability.

Friends who, completely incidentally, had held hands twice in one night, only two days into deciding that they were friends again. It wasn’t complicated unless someone -specifically Agatha's very lovely friend,  Jen- decided to make it complicated. Jen didn’t understand what it meant to reconnect with someone after ten years. She didn’t get that this was normal. Hand holding was friendly. Familiarity was not a crime. And Agatha was absolutely not being delusional about this.

“Come on,” he whined. “You got her at game night. It’s my turn.”

She climbed into the chair Billy had been in, one leg settling underneath her as she leaned forward and rested her elbows on the table.  At some point, Alice had handed over her rose colored sunglasses because now they rested on Sage’s face.

 

It was loud. Not just music loud, but crowded table loud. Jokes overlapped, drink orders were shouted over shoulders, and laughter came in snorts, wheezes, and full body cackles that no one bothered to contain. Teen would not stop talking. Sage kept interrupting him just often enough to tangle the details in his own story, which, bless her, left Agatha free to lean toward Rio with a grin already forming. 

 

They swapped comments, half teases, and dumb observations that got funnier the longer they spiraled. At one point, Rio nearly choked on her beer. At another, Agatha had to grip the edge of the table to keep from doubling over. Across the table, Alice and Jen had fully committed to singing Dancing Queen directly at each other, painfully off key and with way too much eye contact, like they were performing a duet at gunpoint. It was a mess. A perfect one.

 

At some point, Rio and Sage were shouting at each other from across the table about whether or not it was acceptable to send transport for a patient at three in the morning for a non-stat spine x-ray.

 

“No one wants to be dragged out of bed for a routine spine at 3am,” Sage snapped, clearly appalled that this needed to be explained.

 

Rio went right back at her. “If the order’s in, I’m sending for it. I’m not ignoring it just because everyone’s tired.”

 

That should have been it.

 

It wasn’t.

 

Agatha blinked. Then kept blinking as the volume climbed. They were interrupting each other, adding new points, dragging in unrelated grievances from god knows when.

 

Sage leaned in, halfway to launching herself over the table. Rio cracked her knuckles and waved Sage forward like she was welcoming the fight.

 

They fought like sisters. That was the only way Agatha could make sense of it. Not polite or performative, just loud and comfortable and completely without boundaries. Probably the result of too many night shifts stacked side by side, too many shared patients, too many weekends where no one else showed up. 

 

Agatha and Jen still bickered the same way. Still found each other in the middle of a shift to complain, still argued over protocol... or a Bumble match just to pass the time.

 

No one else reacted. Jen took another sip of her drink. Alice and Billy were still wrapped up in whatever nonsense they’d been talking about for the past twenty minutes. 

 

Once it was clear no one else was bothered, Agatha stopped trying to make sense of it. Apparently, this behavior was just part of the atmosphere.

 

Honestly, it was kind of impressive.

 

And it was easily the funniest thing Agatha had seen all night.

 

So when there was barely a breath between points, Agatha leaned in and calmly said, “I mean… Sage has a point.”

 

Agatha didn’t care. She didn’t even know what they were really arguing about anymore. But the way Rio’s head snapped toward her- eyes wide, mouth slightly open, genuinely offended? That made it worth it.

 

So worth it, Agatha had to purse her lips and stare down at the nearly finished whiskey in her hand, still resting on the table, just to keep from laughing.

 

That was when Yelena Belova walked up and stopped in front of their table, directly in front of Sage, and stared at her.

 

Everyone at the table went quiet. Not gradually- instantly. Whatever conversation Billy had been loudly butchering cut off with a weird little choking noise. Jen froze with her glass hovering halfway to her lips, and Alice stopped drumming her fingers against the table and actually turned in her seat and grinned.

Yelena stood there a moment longer, eyes fixed on Sage. 

 

Sage didn’t squirm.

 

Yelena gave the faintest tilt of her head and said, “Buy me a drink.” She immediately turned away and walked off without waiting for a reply.

Rio nodded. “Yeah. I did.”

She swallowed it down, hard, forced a hum, narrowed her eyes, tried to look uncertain. Agatha tried, desperately, to look like she absolutely wasn’t five seconds from blowing up seventeen years of discipline just to chase Rio's smile with her own.

 

The most humiliating part? Agatha wasn’t even drunk. Neither of them were. They were both still nursing the same drink they’d each gotten together earlier, waiting at the bar to order another.

 

There was no blur, no excuse. Just Agatha's own heart, loud and traitorous, the same goddamn thing that had always clawed and screamed for Rio like it didn’t know better. Always pulled toward her. Always made Agatha angle her body just enough to hide the way it wanted more.

 

Seventeen years.

 

The number scraped down the inside of her skull like a dare.

 

It whispered, ‘ haven’t you waited long enough?’

 

Agatha needed Rio to keep talking. Because she wouldn’t ask. She refused to beg.

 

There was still time for Rio to pull back, and Agatha knew it- could feel the possibility of it vibrating in her bones.

 

So Agatha did what she always did. Handed over  the exact opposite of what she meant to the universe, like it was a trade. Like if Agatha pretended hard enough not to want it, just this once, maybe it wouldn’t be taken away.

 

Rio was still looking at her like there was nothing in the world worth hiding from.

 

That made Agatha's stomach drop.

 

The longer Rio chose not say anything, Agatha's heart had felt it had screamed loud enough to be heard, it was losing its voice. It had clawed too hard, too fast, and it didn’t know what to do with the light it found. It flinched from it. Started to bury itself where it had always lived- just beneath Agatha’s ribs, where no one could touch it.

 

Agatha felt her eyes glance away from Rio, flicking past her, reaching for anything solid- any object, any dull fact to ground herself in. A bottle of shelf liquor. A cracked corner in the mirror behind the bar. Something safe.

 

Something that wasn’t Rio Vidal and her roaring silence.

 

Rio spoke.

 

“I didn’t have it in me to be gracious twice.”

 

Agatha’s eyes snapped back to her. She didn’t mean to. It just happened like gravity, like instinct. Blue met brown, and the silence cracked. Agatha bit her tongue. Hard. Forced the sound down before it could betray her.

 

Then Rio asked, “Do you want me to stop?”

 

Switzerland, Agatha reminded herself for what felt like the hundredth time.

 

This was still Switzerland. 

 

Even if it was on fucking fire underneath her feet.

 

“No,” Agatha said, barely more than a breath. “I don’t think I do.”

 

Rio nodded and let out a shaky breath, her whole body vibrating like she was holding too much in too tight a space. The corner of her mouth twitched- almost a smile, but not enough strength behind it to carry it through. “That’s good,” Rio whispered. “That’s really good. You look good, Agatha.” As she said it, she shifted, drawing the side of her body that was still pressed to Agatha’s a half step back. Her eyes dropped, tracking the open line of Agatha’s blazer, the exposed skin beneath it.

 

“Rio.” Agatha’s voice was steady, but everything in it betrayed her. It sounded like control, but it ached like desperation. And Rio- 

 

Rio wasn’t looking anywhere but Agatha’s mouth now.

 

One second. Maybe two. That’s all the time they had left before it happened.

 

“Please let me,” Rio begged.

 

And that was it.

 

That was the moment Agatha heard it- the beginning chords of the Bee Gees More Than a Woman bleeding through the bar speakers.

 

Not even the original song.

 

The fucking Glee cover.

 

Of all the songs in all the bars in the world, it had to be this one,  dripping with sincerity and secondhand embarrassment.

 

Agatha felt her body physically reject it.

 

Because no matter how much she wanted Rio’s mouth on hers -seventeen years of wondering, of pacing the edges of this exact moment- she was not going to kiss her in the middle of a packed bar with a disco heartbreak anthem screeched in a Ryan fucking Murphy musical number.

 

Agatha had limits.

 

She had self respect.

 

If Agatha Harkness was going to ruin seventeen years of perfectly preserved nothing, she was going to do it right. Slowly. Selfishly. With enough detail to replay the memory like a good Catholic in the morning after, when guilt and fear inevitably showed up with a baseball bat and tried to convince her she hadn’t wanted it.

 

So no. Not here.

 

Agatha ripped herself away from Rio in a single breath. A full body decision made in less than a second. No plan. No grace. Just the desperate instinct to escape.



“I’m going outside,” Agatha muttered, already moving- no pause, no explanation. The words fell behind her like dropped coins, left in the faint, humiliating hope someone might bother to pick them up. 

 

Her body reeled from the loss like Agatha ripped it away from something that always belonged to her and now it was missing.

 

The night air hit her face.

 

It wasn’t the slap of reality Agatha had hoped for. It didn’t cool her down. It didn’t fix a thing.

 

Agatha kept walking, rounding the corner of the building, pulse hammering harder with every step. She needed the night to swallow her. Agatha fucking needed the dark to do what she couldn’t.

 

Her back found the brick wall, and she pressed against it like she could force herself to stay still. Like stillness would make her stop feeling it.

 

It was stupid. Loud. Entirely in her chest.

 

Agatha folded her arms across her chest before she could think better of it, pulling the edges of her blazer tight, like that thin layer of fabric might hide her. Might erase the fact that her skin had been seen, wanted, touched without being touched.

 

The heat of Rio’s eyes was gone, but it still burned relentlessly on her skin.

 

And Agatha fucking hated that she missed it.

 

She heard footsteps approaching familiar in a way that made her stomach tighten.

 

They stopped a few feet away.

 

Agatha looked up.

 

Rio.

 

And Agatha realized right then, that she wasn’t going to think about what it meant. Not why now, not whether she’d regret it in the morning. That was for later. All she wanted -all she needed - was to know what Rio tasted like after all this time.

 

Agatha arms fell from her chest. The gesture felt heavier than it should have, like a surrender. Rio’s eyes followed the motion, falling to the strip of skin Agatha no longer bothered to cover. For a moment, Rio didn’t look away. Then she looked right back up to Agatha’s eyes.

 

What comes after, Agatha figures, they could deal with later.



Agatha gave a small nod. Whether it was meant for Rio or for herself, she didn’t know. Her own voice was soft, but steady. “Come here. Please.”

 

She pushed herself off the wall as Rio was already moving toward her. The space between them vanished so quickly it barely felt real. Agatha reached for Rio, fingers cupping Rio’s cheek, needing to close the gap before her brain changed its mind.

 

They collided hard.

 

Agatha fell into Rio and Rio caught Agatha without stumbling back, like she’d been waiting to do that for years. Her hands found Agatha’s hips, then circled around her waist, pulling their bodies into each other. Their mouths found each other in a rush.  It was open from the start, breathless and messy and perfect.

 

The sound that slipped out of Agatha’s mouth was soft but urgent, caught somewhere between a gasp and a groan. Rio answered with one of her own, soft and whined, and the vibration of it lit something deep in Agatha’s spine.

 

Rio’s hand slid up, curling behind her neck, thumb pressing into the curve just beneath her ear as she tilted Agatha closer, deeper. Her mouth was warm, familiar in the way only something long denied could feel. Agatha didn’t hold back. Her lips parted fully, tongue sweeping into Rio’s mouth, tasting her with years of hunger behind it. She tasted beer, breath, the edge of teeth, the softness of longing turned feral.

 

It was everything Agatha imagined and worse. Because now she knew. Now she couldn’t unknow it. Couldn’t untaste Rio. Couldn’t unfeel the way Rio melted into Agatha like she’d been waiting her whole life to do exactly this.

 

Rio tangled her fingers into Agatha’s hair, pulling just enough to guide her, just enough to show Agatha she wasn’t going anywhere. Her kiss was generous but demanding, gentle in a way sleep is to the freezing, impossible to resist, too quiet to fight. Rio let Agatha take, and then asked for more. Her mouth mapped the shape of Agatha’s want, teased apart every breath, every sound, every tremble.

 

And Agatha gave her everything- every sound her mouth could offer, every inch of closeness she had left to give.

 

When they finally broke apart, it wasn’t graceful. Agatha’s breath hitched in her chest, caught between a moan and a laugh. Her head spun. Her legs barely remembered how to hold herself up. Rio leaned in again, forehead brushing gently against Agatha's. They stood there like that for a few moments.

 

Then Rio tilted her chin and kissed Agatha- just once, slower this time. A single press of her lips that might’ve passed for restraint if it hadn’t lingered too long, if it hadn’t said more instead of enough .

 

Agatha’s hand moved instinctively, palm resting flat against Rio’s chest, fingers curling against the heat of her skin, unwillingly twitching because they didn’t want to let go.

 

“We should go back in,” Agatha said, breath shallow and uneven. Even to herself, Agatha sounded entirely unconvinced.

 

And neither of them moved.

 

They didn’t speak.

 

And Agatha -still breathless, still held against Rio with her pulse going absolutely batshit crazy inside her own chest- came to one very clear, very horrifying conclusion: Agatha was absolutely, irreversibly, and possibly cosmically fucked. Not romantically. Not emotionally. Not even sexually, though that suddenly felt like a very short walk. No, this was deeper. Existential. Structural. The kind of fucked that rewrote your internal bylaws and then politely asked you to reread them with feeling.

 

Whatever part of Agatha Harkness had spent seventeen years building a wall around this exact possibility had just watched Agatha obliterate it with her entire mouth open.

 

The fantasy she’d managed to live in, for all of five minutes, had collapsed. 

 

Agatha’s personal Switzerland had lost its neutrality. 

 

It had declared a state of emergency and was actively requesting international aid.

 

And all Agatha could do now was fight not to be buried underneath the rubble.

Agatha went home alone and tried not to let the kiss drown everything else. Tried not to let it bleed into places it didn’t belong.

 

They were friends. The Road was Switzerland. And they kissed. That was all. That had to be all.

 

She didn’t let herself linger on what it meant. She couldn’t. It was too much. So she focused on the mechanics. The press of Rio’s mouth. The feeling of her hands in Agatha’s hair. The slow, certain drag of her tongue. 

 

Definitely not the part where seventeen years of wondering what it might feel like somehow failed to prepare Agatha for the reality of it. Not the part where it ruined every version she’d ever imagined. It left her breathless, undone, aching in a way fantasy never could. It left her starving.

 

Alone in bed, she let her hand slip beneath her waistband. Came quietly, Rio’s name fell from her teeth. That was the deal Agatha made with herself: just this. Just tonight.

 

By morning, Rio would be a story she didn’t tell. The kiss, a lapse in judgment. The jealousy, nothing to examine too closely- just a flicker, a glitch, a moment Rio had no right to claim and Agatha had no business wanting. She’d scrub it from her memory like it didn’t undo her. Like it hadn’t left Agatha wide awake, aching for something she was still pretending not to want.

 

-

 

When Agatha woke up, she didn’t dwell on it. She got up, made her bed, brushed her teeth like it hadn’t happened.

 

She’d kissed Rio. Now she knew what it felt like. She didn’t need to do it again. It didn’t have to mean anything unless she let it, and she wasn’t going to.

 

It didn’t mean they weren’t still trying. Still figuring out how to be in each other’s lives again without making it complicated.

 

They were adults. Capable of being friends. Friends who occasionally made bad decisions, sure, but friends all the same.

 

And Agatha wasn’t going to ruin that just because one of those decisions had left her aching for more.

 

-

 

Two hours later, her phone pinged.

 

Agatha was mid sip, coffee still in her mouth, when she unlocked the screen.

 

Rio: hi

 

She swallowed hard and set the mug down a little too forcefully on the counter.

 

She typed back.

 

Hey.

 

The reply came almost instantly.

 

Rio: are we okay?

 

Agatha exhaled sharply through her nose and fired off a reply with the enthusiasm only panic could produce.

 

Obviously. We’re fine. We’re friends, remember? Everything’s great!!! 

 

Agatha stared at the screen, watching the typing bubbles appear and disappear like Rio couldn’t quite commit. She chewed at her thumbnail, telling herself it wasn’t a big deal. The last thing she needed was for things to get awkward. She still wanted Rio in her life. As a friend, of course.

 

They were trying. They were rebuilding. Two days in wasn’t enough time to screw everything up. Not even for Agatha.

 

Before she could spiral any further, Rio finally responded.

 

A single thumbs up emoji.

 

Agatha blinked at the screen, expression flat.

 

“What the fuck,” she said into the silence of her kitchen. “That’s it?” She slapped the phone face down on the counter.

 

She hadn’t known what to expect, exactly, but it sure as hell wasn’t that. Was she allowed to be mad? Because she was. She absolutely was. Rio kissed her and then-

 

Her phone pinged.

 

Agatha spun around and grabbed it without thinking. 

 

“Thank god,” she whispered, then caught herself. “I mean. Gross.”

 

She unlocked the screen.

 

Rio: you want to get breakfast? i can pick you up. 

 

Good. That’s what Agatha wanted.

 

No drama. No conversation. No rehashing anything that might have happened outside a bar under a streetlight her brain can’t stop replaying.

 

Just breakfast. Just friends.

 

She typed:

 

Sure .

 

And hit send.

 

Rio’s response came in immediately.

 

Rio: cool. send me your address and i’ll head over in 15

 

Agatha sent it, then bolted upstairs.

 

She took the fastest shower she could manage. She threw on jeans and a navy long sleeve with a mock turtleneck. Clean. Neutral. Not trying too hard.

 

She yanked a brush through her hair, checked the mirror, and told herself it was fine.

 

It didn’t matter what she looked like. It was breakfast. With a friend.

 

Ten minutes later, Rio texted that she was outside.

 

Agatha grabbed her purse, took a breath, and paused in front of the foyer mirror. She looked good. Calm. Like someone who wasn’t overthinking any of this.

 

She stepped outside, locked the door behind her, and headed down the porch steps.

 

Rio’s black 4Runner was parked dead center in front of the sidewalk, neat as ever. The windows were tinted too dark to make out much, but Agatha could see the outline of a baseball cap tilted low. Rio’s head was down- probably on her phone. 

 

Agatha squared her shoulders and kept walking toward the car.

 

She rounded the car and slid into the passenger seat.

 

It was exactly what Agatha expected- spotless. It still smelled like a new car, all synthetic leather and obsessive care. A pack of cigarettes was tucked neatly beneath the center console display, and just beneath it, Agatha’s old purple Zippo.

 

Agatha stared at it for a second before looking away.

“Nice car,” Agatha said, casual, clipped.

 

Rio smiled, shifted into drive, and pulled off smoothly. “Thanks. It’s an upgrade from that beat up Beemer I used to drive.”

 

Agatha scoffed. “Please. You loved Tulip.”

 

Rio side eyed her, quiet for half a second. “Yeah. I did,” Rio muttered. “That actually hurt me to say. I take it back. May she rest in peace.”

 

Agatha bit back a grin. “You wrote her a eulogy, didn’t you?”

 

Rio didn’t respond. Which was, frankly, answer enough.

 

“She finally break down on you?” Agatha asked.

 

Rio shook her head. “No. Some jackass rear ended me. Totaled her.” She said it flatly. “I was devastated.”

 

Agatha kept her eyes on the road ahead, lips twitching. “That sucks. When was that?”

 

“About a year ago.”

 

Agatha nodded, still biting back a grin. Rio was dead serious. Mourning the car like it was a person.

 

And honestly? That tracked.

She’d assumed Rio would take them to Sam’s- the old diner across the street from the hospital, the one they always used to go to.

 

But this place was different. Not fancy, just unfamiliar. It hadn’t been here ten years ago when Agatha left, and it definitely wasn’t on Rio’s usual rotation.

 

Rio was a creature of habit. Always had been. She had five or six places and rotated through them like clockwork, always reading the menu ahead of time, always ordering the same thing. She didn’t like surprises. She didn’t take risks.

 

Agatha glanced at the building again.

 

So what the fuck was this?

Rio was supposed to be the same. That was the point. That was the story Agatha had told herself for a decade.

 

That way, Agatha never had to wonder what might’ve happened if Rio had been anything else.

 

And now?

 

Now Agatha wasn’t so sure.

 

And that, whatever that was… felt dangerously close to betrayal.

 

She shoved the door open and scrambled out, trying to make it look effortless. Rio was already at the back of the car, leaning casually against the trunk, waiting.

 

Agatha adjusted her shirt, straightened her posture, and walked over like she hadn’t just spent the last thirty seconds rethinking the last ten years.

 

Everything was fine. She was not thrown off.

 

Not at all.

 

“Let’s go,” Agatha said, striding past Rio and heading straight for the restaurant entrance.

 

Rio followed without a word.

 

At the door, Agatha grabbed the handle, but Rio reached around her and held it open. Agatha walked through like she didn’t notice.

 

She approached the host stand and said, “Two,” before the hostess could ask. The hostess nodded, grabbed two menus, and led them to a booth.

 

They slid into their seats. Agatha set her purse down and reached for the menu, casting a glance at Rio. Not because she cared. She didn’t.

Just out of curiosity.

 

Maybe.

Of course she did.

 

Somehow, that settled Agatha more than it should have. She looked back at her own menu, tension in her shoulders easing.

 

The waitress came by and took their drink orders. When she returned with their drinks, she took their food orders without much small talk.

Lilia Callderu- Agatha was never quite sure whether to call the woman cooky or wispy. Possibly both. The jury had been out for years and showed no signs of returning with a verdict.

 

When Rio was nine, her parents died in a car crash. No next of kin. No one waiting. She cycled through seven foster homes in under a year before landing with Lilia, who, against all odds, kept her. And, eventually, adopted her.

 

“She’s good. Retired five years ago.” Rio said it lightly, her fingers skimming across the table.

 

“Y’all still do Sunday dinners?”

 

When Agatha finally escaped Massachusetts and the chokehold of her mother’s expectations, there was no family waiting on the other side. No home to return to. Holidays were just closed dining halls and couches borrowed from classmates who pitied her more than they liked her.

 

Later, once she had her own apartment, she tried to convince herself it was better that way. No obligations. No travel. Just her and a pile of takeout containers, watching the world celebrate through double paned glass. It was fine. Manageable, even. Loneliness had rules, and she followed them.

 

Then she met Jen. And, inevitably, Rio.

 

Rio had invited her to Sunday dinner once. Agatha had almost said no, out of habit. But she went. Lilia had asked about her family that night, not prying, just curious. Agatha had shrugged and said there wasn’t one. That was all it took.

 

No one made a speech or carved her name into a chair, but after that, there was always a place set for Agatha. She started showing up on Sundays. Then holidays. Birthdays that weren’t hers. At some point, Agatha stopped flinching when coworkers asked where she was going for Thanksgiving. 

 

Agatha never called it home, but it was the closest thing she’d ever had to one. And it was enough. More than enough.

 

And then she met Wanda.

 

It happened gradually, the way most things do when you think you’ll get another chance. 

 

Just a few missed dinners. Conflicts, scheduling, the pull of a new life arranging itself around her. Wanda didn’t ask where she spent her Sundays, and Agatha didn’t offer. She told herself it was fine. That she’d go next week. Or the one after that.

 

By then, Agatha belonged elsewhere. She was someone else’s wife, part of someone else’s plan. It was natural, she reasoned. What people did when they fell in love- rearranged their lives, let a few things go.

 

Rio nodded. “Sage and I work every Sunday, so we moved it to Tuesdays. But yeah, still happens.”

 

Something in Agatha lurched to a sudden, terrifying halt. 

 

Agatha blinked.

 

Sage and I. 

 

Since when did Sage factor into Lilia’s dinners?

 

The realization hit Agatha in the gut- sharp, specific, and quietly fucking devastating. She had missed something. Something important. And worse than that, she wasn’t sure she had the right to ask for it back.

 

“Sage?” Agatha asked, trying to sound neutral.

Foster fails.
