“By the time Lilia adopted her, you were already in Chicago. We hadn’t spoken in months. And it felt too late. Too weird.” Rio gave a breath of a laugh, humorless. “What was I supposed to do, Agatha? Reach out and say, ‘Hey, remember that foster kid I never mentioned? She’s still here. She’s basically family now. Thought you should know’?”

 

Every word out of Rio’s mouth sounded reasonable. A perfectly logical, deeply human mistake.

 

But Agatha still wanted to scream.

 

Agatha shook her head. “You knew what that place meant to me. What Lilia meant to me. You knew. You just didn’t want to deal with what it might’ve meant if I still cared.”

 

Rio flinched at that, just barely, but Agatha saw it.

 

“I didn’t mean to-”

 

Agatha scoffed. “You didn’t mean to,” she repeated. “That’s the problem with you. You never mean to do anything, and people still get hurt.”

 

Rio swallowed hard. “You’re right,” she said. “You had every right to know. And I fucked up. I’m sorry, Agatha. I really am.”

 

Well. Agatha got her apology. Rio actually took accountability for once, which was- miraculous, honestly. One small miracle in the timeline of their spectacularly dysfunctional history.

 

She was still pissed. That wasn’t changing anytime soon. Agatha fully intended to hold onto the narrative that Rio was completely in the wrong and maybe also the actual devil. But for now? She was over this fucking conversation.

 

“Noted,” was all Agatha said, then took a long sip from her straw and turned to stare out the window.

 

“Are you still mad at me?” Rio asked, softly.

 

Agatha looked over, and there it was. That face. Those goddamn eyes- big, brown, and full of guilt and whatever the hell softness Rio always used to pull out when she felt bad about something but didn’t know how to fix it.

 

Naturally, Agatha felt like shit. Because seeing Rio sad always made her feel like shit. It was like being asked to walk barefoot across miles of legos and pretend it wasn’t painful as fuck. 

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “No.” 

 

She grabbed her drink, took a sip, looked back out the window.

 

“But for the record,” Agatha muttered, “you’re still an asshole.”

 

“That’s fair.”

 

Agatha could feel Rio watching her.

 

“Just act normal before I change my mind.”

 

Their food came not long after, and the conversation shifted with it. They didn’t force it- they just moved on from the heavy stuff.

 

They talked. About nothing, mostly. About the waitress’s attitude. About how Rio still couldn’t order anything without turning it into a ten step customization. Agatha made fun of her for it. Rio told her to shut up. Agatha smirked into her drink and took it as a win.

 

It got easier as they went. Not perfect. But easier.

 

And maybe it was going too well. So well that Agatha felt the familiar itch creep in that made her want to ruin it before it got comfortable. Before it could start feeling like safety again. Especially when she caught herself looking at Rio’s mouth, thinking how it looked better last night. Right after they’d kiss.

 

Agatha stabbed her fork at her plate and asked, like it was no big deal, “You date anyone while I was in Chicago?”

 

Rio didn’t look thrown. She wiped her mouth, slid her plate out of the way, and smiled.

 

“Not seriously,” Rio said with a shrug. “But a woman has needs.”

 

Agatha grimaced inwardly. Of course Rio had flings. She always had flings. Casual. Disposable. Easy to laugh about the next morning.

 

God, it was pathetic how that still managed to sting.

 

“Classy,” Agatha muttered, trying to swallow the bite of food she suddenly wanted absolutely nothing to do with.

 

Rio raised an eyebrow, but didn’t take the bait. Just watched her for a beat, then leaned back and said, “Alright. My turn.”

 

Agatha swallowed hard, eyes narrowing. “Your turn for what?”

 

Rio rested her arms on the table and folded her hands like they were settling in for a conversation she’d been waiting to have. “You asked me a question. Seems fair I get to ask one in return.”

 

Agatha leaned back, arms crossed. “Yeah? Better make it count.”

 

Rio met her eyes and didn’t look away. “Why did you and Wanda get divorced?”

 

Agatha groaned- loudly, unapologetically. “God.”

 

-

 

It wasn’t a simple answer. Nothing ever was with Agatha.

 

It hadn’t been some big, dramatic moment that made Agatha realize she was done.

 

It was a sweatshirt.

 

Ugly. Faded. A thing Rio had tossed her once, without thinking, back when things were easier. It had lived in the back of the closet for years, buried between clothes Agatha never wore but couldn’t let go of. It was the only thing in that apartment that still felt like hers. Not because it was from Rio, but because it was untouched by Wanda.

 

Sure, Agatha had never fully quit smoking. That was the one thing she held onto to keep some version of herself intact. But even that had been touched by the life she was in, folded into secrecy, kept out of sight. It wasn’t really untouched.

 

But that sweatshirt was.

 

Until one day, it wasn’t. 

 

It was just gone.

 

Agatha had asked Wanda if she’d seen it. Wanda had smiled and said, “Oh, that old thing? I donated it last week. You never wore it.”

 

That was it. Just another edit made on Agatha’s behalf. And Agatha had smiled, nodded, said it was fine. Then went into the bathroom, shut the door, and sat on the floor until her hands stopped shaking.

 

Wanda had taken so much from her. Not in obvious ways. Never all at once. It was always framed as care, as compromise. Change this. Adjust that. Make it easier, softer, more manageable. And Agatha did. She moved. She bent. She swallowed things whole.

 

Then to top it off, Wanda had looked at the one thing Agatha had managed to keep for herself and saw nothing worth keeping.

 

That’s what Agatha couldn’t forgive.

 

It wasn’t a revelation. It was a dull kind of disgust that settled under her skin and stayed there.

 

She didn’t leave right away. She made dinner. She went to work. She sent polite texts, cleared the dishwasher. She tried not to look at the empty space in the closet. The paperwork came a few weeks later, and she filled it out without thinking, as if it were just one more thing to be done.

 

Irreconcilable differences.

 

It sounded reasonable. Like two people had simply drifted apart in a way that couldn’t be fixed. And maybe, in the most technical sense, that was true. But it didn’t come close to explaining the years she spent whittling herself down into something smaller just to make it work.

 

There wasn’t a fight. There were forms. A few tense days. Logistics.

 

Wanda kept asking what had changed. Agatha never answered. Because it wasn’t one moment. It was everything. Every compromise, every swallowed part of herself that was dismissed as love.

 

The sweatshirt just made it too obvious to ignore.

 

-

 

Agatha blinked. Her fingers curled around her Diet Coke. She looked at Rio, cleared her throat and said, “I filed under irreconcilable differences. It sounded better than saying I couldn’t remember the last time I felt like a person in my own life.”

 

Rio raised an eyebrow. “That’s it?”

 

Agatha nodded. “Box was right there. Felt rude not to check it.”

 

Rio let out a quiet laugh, shaking her head. “Okay.”

 

“What?”

 

“Nothing. I just always figured if you two ever split, the reasons would include ‘chronic rudeness’ and ‘a deeply suspicious relationship with wine.’”

 

Agatha snorted. “Makes enough sense.”

 

“Right?” Rio said, grinning. That gap in her teeth was showing, and Agatha’s heart flipped in a way she chose to ignore. “But I must say, I do have quite the soft spot for Agnes.”

 

Agatha groaned and immediately threw a home fry at her. Rio dodged it without moving much at all, still grinning.

 

“I’m just saying,” Rio said, unfazed, “She had a crush on me, you know.”

 

Agatha scoffed. “She did not.”

 

“Oh, she absolutely did,” Rio said. “Two and a half glasses in and I was suddenly being told I had the best hands on the East Coast.”

 

Agatha laughed and grabbed another home fry to toss. “That never happened.”

 

Rio caught it midair with one hand and looked far too pleased with herself. “It did, actually. And for the record, she matched with me on Bumble just a few days ago.”

 

That stalled Agatha for half a second. She pressed her lips together like she was trying not to react, but the smile tugging at the corner of her mouth gave her away. Across the table, Rio just tilted her head and stared, tongue tucked into her cheek, wearing the exact kind of face that said, go ahead, try and talk your way out of that one.

 

Agatha exhaled through her nose and gave a slight shake of her head. “Yeah, well. She has issues.”

 

Rio shot back, “She has taste.”

 

Agatha didn’t look at her. “She tried to climb into your lap in the middle of a Chili’s.”

 

Rio sat up a little, eyes wide with conviction. “Oh, you mean only the greatest restaurant in the U.S. of A.? We were at Chili’s, Agatha. Chili’s. It was the closest I’ve ever come to a religious experience, and I wanted to marry her on the spot.”

 

Agatha stared at her, genuinely at a loss. “Okay. Your obsession with Chili’s has always been fucking weird. ‘The greatest restaurant in the U.S. of A.?’ Do you understand how insane that sounds out loud?”

 

Rio looked offended that Agatha had even asked such a question. “It’s not my fault this country peaked at the Triple Dipper and free, never ending chips and salsa.”

 

Agatha blinked, slowly. “Jesus Christ.”

 

Rio nodded. “Exactly.”

 

The conviction alone should’ve been enough to roll her eyes and move on. Instead, Agatha found herself staring- irritated, mostly. And for reasons that didn’t hold up to any logic at all, she wanted to kiss Rio. Terribly.

 

Before Agatha could spiral, the waitress appeared beside them with a practiced smile and set the check on the edge of the table- completely oblivious to the fact that Agatha was exactly one second away from making a very poor decision because of Rio’s bizarre obsession with Chili’s.

 

Rio grabbed the check and pulled her wallet from the back pocket of her jeans. She was already moving like she’d planned to cover it the whole time, before Agatha could even think to offer.

 

“Don’t make it weird,” Rio said. “Even though, morally, I should absolutely make you pay for the Chili’s slander.”

 

Agatha didn’t fight her on it.

 

She just watched Rio slide the card into the check sleeve, still clearly pouting over the alleged Chili’s slander.

 

God, she’s so fucking annoying.

 

Agatha wanted to kiss her so badly it made her jaw ache.

 

-

 

It wasn’t perfect. The morning had been weird and tense and heavier than it should’ve been. But somehow, they’d made it through. Laughed. Talked like people who knew how to talk to each other.

 

And that felt... good. Annoyingly good.

 

So when Rio pulled up in front of Agatha’s house and shifted the car into park, Agatha felt that sinking feeling she used to get every time one of them left too early.

 

They’d spent years knowing each other down to the breath, and for a few brief minutes, that had resurfaced. And now Agatha didn’t want to be left alone with it.

 

“You can come in, if you want.”

 

Because it’s easier than saying she didn’t hate the morning.

 

Rio glanced over, one eyebrow barely raised. “Yeah?” she asked, quiet, like she was making sure Agatha wasn’t about to take it back.

 

Agatha didn’t answer.

 

So Rio nodded once. “Okay. Yeah. I want.”

 

They didn’t need to make it a thing.

 

Sometimes, showing up was enough.

 

-

 

They stepped into Agatha’s house, and Rio started snooping immediately, eyes roaming, hands already picking things up like she was on a guided tour with no guide.

 

“I’m going upstairs to change,” Agatha said, already unbuttoning her jeans. “I’d rather get hit by a car than lounge in denim.”

 

She paused on the steps and glanced back. “Want a pair of shorts?”

 

“Sure,” Rio called, distracted- already flipping through Agatha’s mail like she paid the bills.

 

Agatha didn’t even bother trying to stop her. “Knock yourself out. Let me know if you find anything interesting… Maybe a coupon.”

 

Rio made a noise that might’ve been a laugh. Agatha just shook her head and headed upstairs, leaving Rio to commit fraud in peace.

 

Agatha pulled on a light blue tank top with thin straps and a pair of blue and white pinstriped boxers. She grabbed a pair of shorts from the dresser for Rio before heading downstairs.

 

She found Rio standing in front of the television, idly scrolling through what looked like an endless lineup of streaming options.

 

“Find anything interesting?” Agatha asked as she crossed the room.

 

“Your mail’s depressing,” Rio said without looking back. When she finally did turn around, her eyes barely skimmed over Agatha before she reached for the shorts and handed over the remote. 

 

“I’d tell you where the bathroom is, but I’m guessing you already know!” Agatha shouted after her, watching as Rio headed confidently down the hall toward the half bath without needing directions.

 

Rio’s classic evil little cackles echoed back in response.

 

Agatha shook her head, already smiling.

 

She sank into the corner of the couch -the L-shaped part she always claimed- and turned on a movie, pretending it was a random pick. It wasn’t. It was The Proposal . A rom-com she loved far more than she’d ever admit, and had seen enough times to mouth the lines word for word.

 

Rio returned a few minutes later, now in the shorts but still wearing her layered long sleeve under her t-shirt. She’d taken off the baseball cap, letting her hair fall messily around her face.

 

Rio came around the couch and glanced at the screen. “Love this movie,” she said, dropping into a spot two cushions down. She tucked her legs underneath her, body angled slightly toward Agatha.

 

They weren’t paying much attention to the movie. It had barely started -maybe five minutes in- when Agatha asked if Rio wanted a beer. Rio said sure. Agatha got up, grabbed two from the fridge, and handed one over.

 

They started talking. About nothing, really. Nothing that used to fill entire afternoons. At some point, the conversation swerved. Agatha wasn’t sure how they got there, but suddenly Rio was saying she’d never had her ears pierced.

 

Agatha blinked at her. “What, ever?”

 

Rio shrugged. “Nope.”

 

Agatha, who had more holes in her ears than she could keep track of, narrowed her eyes. Sometimes she wore earrings in all of them, sometimes just one or two. It depended on the day. Or her mood. Or the level of petty defiance required.

 

She sipped her beer. “You seem like someone who’s afraid of needles.”

 

Rio rolled her eyes. “I’m not.”

 

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “Are you sure?”

 

“I’m not!”

 

And that was all it took. Agatha sat up a little straighter.

 

“Let me pierce your ears, then.”

 

She said it casually, like it was no big deal. She knew how. She’d done her own years ago, in a bathroom mirror with shaking hands and too much eyeliner. When your mother is Evanora Harkness, you learn quickly what will set her off. Piercing her own ears had been the fastest way to start a fire without lighting a match. The memory still made her smile.

 

Rio didn’t hesitate. Of course she didn’t. She grinned, wide and a little chaotic, the same way she always had when she’d already decided on something.

 

Rio lifted her beer slightly. “Let’s pierce my ears, sweetheart.”

 

Naturally, Agatha had supplies. She kept things like that around in case she got bored or curious or restless. It wasn’t a surprise. What was surprising was how still Rio sat while Agatha cleaned her earlobes with isopropyl alcohol.

 

She’d knelt in front of Rio to mark both ears evenly, gauging the angles with practiced eyes. But when she looked up to double check, she faltered.

 

Rio was staring at her. Not in amusement or challenge- but with this quiet, thoughtful sort of focus. Like she was trying to memorize her.

 

Agatha froze, just for a second. She coughed a small laugh and cleared her throat, willing the warmth rushing to her face to go unnoticed. Agatha pretended she didn’t know how obvious it was when she blushed.

 

She made sure everything was right- no crooked holes or infections under her watch. She was a nurse, after all. Sterility wasn’t optional. Gloves on. Supplies prepped. Rio’s hair was pulled back in a high ponytail to keep it out of the way, and Agatha had already broken a bar of soap into chunks- just the right size to hold behind each ear for support.

 

Rio held out her hand and flicked open Agatha’s old purple Zippo. Agatha sterilized the needle in the flame.

 

“Don’t move,” she said, steady. “I’m gonna stab you on the count of three.”

 

“One. Two-”

 

Agatha pierced Rio’s ear on two.

 

Rio let out a scream -high pitched and dramatic, like she was being murdered- and jerked just slightly.

 

But Agatha didn’t flinch. She’d spent over a decade in the NICU, poking squirmy little creatures who cried and wailed and made everything ten times harder. She didn’t mind. She was used to it. She was good at this.

 

And besides, Rio had asked for it.

 

Agatha moved with the small jolt of Rio’s body, steadying herself until she was sure Rio wouldn’t flinch again. Then she sat back on her heels and smiled- breath catching a little as she took in the stunned expression on Rio’s face.

 

“See?” she said, smug and breathless. “That wasn’t so bad.”

 

Rio stared at her, mouth hanging open, eyes wide in full betrayal. It was the most are you fucking serious look Agatha had ever seen.

 

“You said on three!”

 

Agatha barely held back a laugh, biting her lip as she reached for the jewelry. “I felt you tense as soon as I said two. I didn’t have a choice.”

 

“It hurt, ” Rio snapped, voice climbing into a register that bordered on toddler level indignation. The only thing missing was throwing herself dramatically to the floor.

 

Agatha just hummed in fake sympathy as she swapped out the needle for the earring- a small black diamond.

 

“We don’t have to do the other one,” Agatha gently added, sliding the back of the earring into place with careful fingers.



“No- I want the other one done,” Rio shot back, just as upset that Agatha had dared suggest quitting in the middle of a mission.

 

“You sure?”

 

“Do it now. Actually-” Rio paused, narrowing her eyes. “On three.”

 

Agatha held up her hands in mock surrender. “Okay. On three.”

 

She prepped the second ear just as carefully as the first- soap, flame, steady fingers. Then she leaned in again, voice calm.

 

“One. Two-”

 

Rio’s eyes squeezed shut.

 

“Three.”

 

And just like that, it was done.

 

Agatha disposed of the needle first, carrying it to the kitchen where she kept a small sharps container tucked behind the sink. She dropped it in with a soft click, then peeled off her gloves.

 

She crossed back into the living room and sank onto her knees between Rio’s legs. Her hands came to rest on the tops of Rio’s bare thighs, fingers brushing the soft skin there like they weren’t sure what they were allowed to touch.

 

Rio was trying not to pout. 

 

And God, Agatha had missed her. Missed her like it was a chronic ache. It settled in the way she would reach for someone in her dreams and wake up empty handed. In the way she would avoid certain songs. Certain memories she didn’t trust herself to touch without it stinging.

 

Because it wasn’t just missing a person. It was missing Rio . The expressions she made when she was pretending not to pout, the way she turned toward Agatha even in silence, the reckless affection that always came a few seconds before Agatha could brace for it.

 

Agatha didn’t have the words for what that did to her.

 

And suddenly, she wasn’t braced at all. Rio had her arms around her, pulling her in, and Agatha let it happen.

 

The hug was awkward -Rio perched on the couch, Agatha still kneeling on the floor- but somehow it didn’t feel that way. It just felt like them . A little off center, but holding anyway.

 

Agatha let herself melt into it, her arms slipping under Rio’s shoulders, hands pressing gently against her back.

 

She didn’t say anything. Just leaned in  and tucked her face into the curve of Rio’s shoulder. It was warm, familiar, safe. Rio still smelled like fresh laundry. And when the smile crept up on Agatha’s face, uninvited and too big to hide, she pressed it into Rio’s shoulder, and let it disappear there.

 

Like a secret. Just between them. 

 

“I really missed you, Agatha,” Rio mumbled into the side of her hair.

 

Agatha closed her eyes. “Yeah,” she whispered. “Me too.” It was all she could manage.

 

Rio pulled back after a moment and gave her a small, crooked smile. Then she closed her eyes and tilted her head to show off both ears.

 

“Well?” Rio asked. “Do I look cooler now?”

 

Agatha huffed a laugh. “You look fine. Go check the mirror if you need the ego boost.”

 

Rio grinned like that was exactly what she planned to do. She stood up, padded over to the foyer mirror, tilted her head this way and that, and hummed thoughtfully.

 

Agatha shifted on the floor, turning to rest her back against the couch.

 

“Yeah,” Rio said, nodding at her reflection. “I definitely shouldn’t have let you do this. I’m gonna be even more of a babe magnet now. You might have to fight the ladies off me.”

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I’ll start training immediately.”

 

Rio walked back and dropped onto the floor right next to Agatha, close enough their knees brushed. She picked up her beer, took a sip, and squinted at the TV. Agatha caught the way her eyes narrowed slightly. Then, without any warning, she turned to Agatha and asked, dead serious:

 

“Do you mow your own lawn?” 

 

The question was so out of place, so deeply Rio, that Agatha couldn’t help but laugh. Loud and disbelieving, the sound burst out of her before she had a chance to rein it in.

 

“Be serious,” Agatha said, shaking her head. “I’ve built my entire personality around never touching a lawn mower. I pay the neighbor’s kid.”

 

Rio grunted and turned back to the screen, unimpressed. “Fire him,” she muttered into her bottle before taking another sip. “And please clarify if he’s also the one responsible for turning your flower beds into a botanical crime scene.”

 

Agatha whipped her head toward her, eyebrows raised. “You’re very invested in this for someone who doesn’t live here.”

 

“I’m serious. Fire him. He’s doing a terrible job. Tell him he’s seventeen and it’s not too late to pursue literally any other calling.”

 

“He’s thirteen,” Agatha corrected. “And I’m not exactly drowning in other options willing to do it for fifteen bucks and a Gatorade.”

 

Rio gave her a long, almost theatrical sigh and rolled her eyes as if the answer had been obvious from the start. “I would,” she said. Her hand came to rest on Agatha’s thigh. 

 

Agatha didn’t move. She didn’t even breathe for a second, just let the warmth of it sink in.

 

“Free of charge,” Rio continued, still looking at the screen. “Out of pity. And to spare you from being the reason the neighborhood Facebook group starts posting pictures of your yard with captions like ‘Thoughts and prayers.’”

 

Agatha didn’t even try to hold back the snort that slipped out. Rio looked at her and grinned, wide and self satisfied, and it made Agatha’s heart do a somersault in her chest.

 

“It’s not that bad,” Agatha muttered, eyes drifting back to the screen, though her focus didn’t follow. Her fingers traced the length of Rio’s arm without much thought.

 

Rio gave a lazy shrug and made a quiet, noncommittal sound. “It’s not hopeless,” she said, voice low. “Just embarrassing.”

 

She turned her palm upward in Agatha’s lap, a small but unmistakable gesture that told Agatha not to stop. So Agatha didn’t. Her fingers kept moving, tracing gently along the inside of Rio’s forearm.

 

They sat in the quiet for a little while, both of them watching the screen without really seeing it. Agatha’s fingers kept brushing slowly back and forth along Rio’s arm. No teasing. No commentary. Just the hum of closeness that neither of them seemed in a rush to break.

 

Eventually, Rio sat up a little straighter, shifting her body toward Agatha. One elbow came up to rest on the couch as she leaned her head into her hand, completely at ease. Agatha’s hand, the one that had been stroking along Rio’s arm, fell to her thigh instead, unsure of where else to go now that it wasn’t following the line of Rio’s skin.

 

Then Rio brought her other hand up and poked lightly at Agatha’s chest. “Lucky for you,” Rio said, a smile tugging at the corner of her mouth, “you know someone with a criminally underappreciated green thumb and excellent taste, who just so happens to be sitting right here.”

 

Rio and her fucking green thumb.

 

Rio’s apartment had always been full of plants. They were never loud. Never wild. One in a corner, another near the light. Something green and reaching on the balcony. Her space had always looked alive, in the most deliberate way. 

 

And somehow, her plants had ended up in Agatha’s space too.

 

It hadn’t been a conversation. It wasn’t a gift. It was a slow collection. A potted plant on the kitchen counter. A plant in a hanging basket hooked on Agatha’s balcony one afternoon and never taken back. Agatha hadn’t asked for them. Rio hadn’t asked to leave them. But there they were.

 

And Agatha let them stay. She watered them. Moved them around when they got too much sun. Pretended it wasn’t a thing.

 

Rio even used to hang eucalyptus in her shower. Which meant, eventually, Agatha did it too. At first it was because it smelled nice. Then because she got used to it. Even in Chicago, she’d kept it going. Currently, Agatha had some hanging in her bathroom upstairs.

 

It was just a habit Agatha hadn’t gotten around to breaking. A habit her body remembered, even when her pride didn’t want to.

 

And now Rio was propped up on one elbow, looking at Agatha- smirking, poking a finger to Agatha’s chest like she knew what beat there, and had no idea it had always been hers. That somehow, she’d taken up residence there without ever realizing it.

 

But Rio always had a way of doing that.

 

She planted, let things grow. Left parts of herself behind the way she used to leave behind plants: A pot on the counter. A hanging basket on the balcony. 

 

Harmless, until they weren’t. Until one day you looked around and realized they’d taken over the place. Thriving. Blooming. Tangling themselves into corners Agatha had never meant to share.

 

“You offering to mow my lawn for free?” Agatha whispered, after tracing every piece of Rio that had outlived her absence.

 

It was the only thing she could come up with that didn’t involve her heart falling out of her mouth and straight into Rio’s hands.

 

Rio moved the hand still resting against Agatha’s chest, lifted it, and gently tucked a piece of hair behind Agatha’s ear. 

 

“I can do more than that,” Rio muttered, barely above a whisper. “Clear out the flowerbeds. Pull up the old roots. Put down new ones. Something bright. Azaleas, maybe.”

 

As Rio spoke, her hand slipped from Agatha’s cheek and settled gently over her chest again. She let it rest there for a moment, closed loosely into a fist.

 

Then, again with a single finger, she tapped twice against Agatha’s heart. Like she was answering for all the times she hadn’t known what she was touching.

 

Oh.

 

So that’s what it was like- an offer wrapped in a metaphor, quiet enough not to spook Agatha. A small touch, planted with intention. A gesture that left no room for misreading.

 

She had spent so long waiting to hear it- then longer convincing herself she never would. And now that it had been offered, gently and without condition, she didn’t know how to trust it. It didn’t feel like a lie. That was the worst part. It felt real.

 

But seventeen years had taught Agatha how to speak around what she meant. How to make herself small enough to survive disappointment. How to twist her truth into something more manageable, easier to walk away from.

 

“The soil’s been neglected, you know,” Agatha murmured, almost to herself. “Things don’t root easy after that. And it’s hard to tell, sometimes. What’s dead and what’s just taking its time… And sometimes it…  sometimes it grows strange. Reaches in the wrong directions. Starts needing things it doesn’t know how to ask for.”

 

Agatha paused. It should’ve ended there. It would’ve, if she were braver.

 

Agatha looked away and added, “Probably not worth the effort if it doesn’t know what to do with the sunlight.” She reached for a loose thread on her rug, tugging at it gently.

 

It was second nature to twist instinct into dismissal, building exits into every sentence just in case Agatha needed to run. The words had left her too easily, like her mouth still hadn’t gotten the memo that she didn’t want to be misunderstood anymore.

 

That was the problem.

 

Because what Agatha had meant, if she were the kind of person who said what she meant, was simple.

 

Don’t hold me at face value when I say stupid shit. Especially when it sounds like I’m pushing you away.

 

But what Agatha had said instead, was that it wasn’t worth the effort.

 

Rio had always been good at showing up, at presence, at staying close. But she’d never been good at hearing what Agatha couldn’t say directly. Their language always ended up lost in translation. 

 

And now Agatha had to wait and see if Rio heard her anyway.

 

Rio’s thumb brushed lightly once across Agatha’s sternum. 

 

“That’s okay,” Rio said quietly. “I’ll try again tomorrow.”

 

The words rang familiar in Agatha’s ears.

 

Agatha hadn’t known what to do with them before. She hadn’t let herself believe they meant anything more than what they said. Hadn’t let herself linger. It was easier to chalk it up to Rio being her usual brand of ridiculous- dramatic flirting, cryptic phrasing, her emotional sleight of hand. Easier for Agatha to roll her eyes than consider the possibility that any of it was sincere.

 

This time, though, Agatha heard it differently. 

 

Rio had never just meant tomorrow.

 

She meant as long as it took.

 

Agatha tore her gaze from the thread and looked at Rio, startled by finally being heard and by the way honesty had replaced the face of fear.

 

Agatha’s throat felt too tight, her chest too full, but the word still found its way out.

 

“Okay,” Agatha whispered.

 

It was the only word she could come up with that gave Rio permission to keep showing up. And Agatha needed her to keep showing up- even when Agatha said the wrong thing. Especially then. Because Agatha wouldn't mean it. She never had.

 

And somehow, Rio had heard that. Heard it beneath the noise, beneath the old habits Agatha hadn’t quite yet figured out how to kill.

 

Rio nodded a little. “Okay,” she whispered back.

 

And that was it.

 

Rio shifted, settled back against the couch the way they had before, eyes on the screen, saying nothing else. Agatha turned back too.

 

She swallowed hard and blinked a few times, willing the lump in her throat to disappear before it embarrassed her. Seventeen years of tension, of space, of assumptions. Of telling herself Rio wouldn’t change because she never had. That no one could be that stubborn and still become someone new.

 

But Rio had. 

 

And Agatha was still learning how to move again. Still tangled in what those seventeen years had done to her. Still trying to figure out what kind of version of herself could exist now, after some of the dust had settled.

 

But Rio was patient. Not hovering. Not pushing. Just there. And she would wait. For as long as Agatha needed her to.

 

And for now, that was enough.

Chapter Notes

Hello! Yes. I told myself I’d wait until AAA week was over to post this chapter, but, as it turns out, I have zero impulse control. So here we are.

The amount of plant googling I’ve had to do for this fic alone has MADE ME SICK

And finally, a big thank you to Renee Rapp’s song Swim and Monday's NYT Connections for inspiring certain parts of this chapter :) it's tooth rotting.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha woke up to her alarm at noon, groaning as she smacked her phone off the nightstand and blinked up at the ceiling. First shift of three. That meant she had just enough time to get her life in order before surrendering it to the hospital for the next few nights.



She had about four hours to shower, grocery shop, and maybe meal prep for the weekend if she was feeling ambitious. With any luck, Agatha could finish early and squeeze in a solid hour or two of unproductive couch rotting before having to pull herself together for work.



Agatha swung her legs over the side of the bed and sat there for a moment. Waking up always felt like a negotiation. Her body usually cooperated. Her brain, however, always took a bit more convincing.

 

With one long, obnoxious groan, Agatha leaned over, grabbed her phone from where it had slipped off the nightstand, and trudged downstairs.

 

On her way to the kitchen, Agatha passed the guest bathroom, when a sliver of light spilling into the hallway made her pause. The light was left on from the night before.



She reached in, hand automatically going for the light switch, but stopped short when she saw a sticky note that was stuck perfectly to the edge of the mirror- purple, small, and unmistakably Rio’s handwriting.



Agatha’s stomach did a stupid, flip thing.



She stepped fully into the bathroom and peeled the note from the mirror, careful not to wrinkle it.



 

Sunlight’s overrated. I’ll plant shade lovers. They still bloom… And are very much worth the effort 🖤

                                                   -  R



 

Agatha stared at the sticky note.



“Jesus Christ.” She mumbled, reading it again for the third time.

 

Agatha read it again. Then once more, just to be sure it still made her stomach twist in that way she hated.

 

Great. Now she was smiling.

 

Only a little. Just enough to be annoyed at herself.

Agatha slid the sticky note carefully into the pocket of her sweatpants. Then she turned off the bathroom light and headed to the kitchen.

 

She dropped a pod into the Keurig and hit the button. While it churned to life, she pulled out her phone. She typed slowly, letting her thumb hover for a second before finishing the sentence.

 

How are your ears feeling?

 

Agatha hit send and locked her phone.

 

The Keurig finished with a final sputter and she drank it standing by the counter, not bothering to sit or pretend she had more time than she did. She had work tonight. A grocery run to fit in before that.

 

Once the cup was empty, Agatha set it in the sink and headed upstairs.

 

Somewhere in between tugging off her sweatshirt and reaching for a towel, she pulled the sticky note from her pocket and, without thinking much about it, stuck it to the bathroom mirror. The glass was already starting to fog. She pressed the paper flat with the heel of her hand, just enough to make sure it stayed.

 

By the time she stepped back, her reflection was already starting to blur, and the note had become the clearest thing in the bathroom.

 

Agatha didn’t think about it.

Agatha got all her shit done and collapsed into her sacred rot time on the couch- blanket slipping off her legs, some Bravo monstrosity droning in the background, and no plans to move unless her house caught on fire.

 

Her phone buzzed twice against her thigh.

 

Two notifications. Both from Rio.

 

The first was a photo- taken from a ridiculous angle, Rio’s arm stretched high. She was still in bed, hair twisted into a slept-on ponytail, one eye shut, head tilted just enough to show off one of her new piercings. She wore a faded black t-shirt with Audrey II from Little Shop of Horrors grinning across the front.

 

Of course. The carnivorous plant thing. Agatha had no idea when the obsession started, but she’d learned not to ask questions about Rio’s taste for morally ambiguous flora.

 

Beneath the photo:

Agatha: Careful. I’ll take you up on that.

 

Rio: on second thought… i think i’m good :) 

Rio: save your energy. once these piercings debut i’m expecting at least three brawls and one marriage proposal by midnight.

 

Agatha: Better make sure the ER is prepped. I’ve got excellent aim🔪🔪🩸🩸

 

Rio: so hot

 

Agatha was still deciding whether or not to respond to Rio’s text when the most cursed name in her contacts covered her screen.

 

Wanda M.

 

Agatha loudly groaned into the air and rolled onto to her stomach, limbs sprawled across the couch, irritated that Wanda still had access to her number and that she’d interrupted what had been, up until now, a very decent evening before work.

 

She let it ring. She hadn’t spoken to Wanda in months. She’d ignored the last round of erratic texts and saw no reason to reward this latest intrusion with an answer. 

 

Still, Agatha wasn’t sure how close she was to actually blocking her. The impulse came very often, followed by the stupid moral calculus of whether thirteen years entitled Wanda to one final conversation. Something along the lines of: Free me from whatever this fucking post divorce purgatory is before I scorch what little civility we have left.

 

The second call came a minute later. Same name. Same number. Same rising pressure at the back of her skull. Agatha let it ring again while she shoved her face into a pillow and yelled until the sound scraped her throat.

 

When it stopped, she didn’t move. She waited, breathing through her teeth, hoping that was the end of it.

 

It buzzed again. Then again. Two short, separate jolts. Not a call. Two texts.

 

Agatha decided to check, not because she thought Wanda had suddenly learned impulse control, but because there was a chance it wasn’t her. A small, stupid, wishful chance.

 

Agatha knew better. But she checked anyway.

 

Much to her disappointment, it was exactly who she thought it was.

 

Wanda.

 

The second the pictures loaded, Agatha knew they were from Jen’s Facebook. 70s Night at The Witches’ Road. Wanda hadn’t even bothered to crop them.

 

Sloppy.

 

The first photo was a group shot. Everyone else was smiling for the camera, drinks held up, arms slung around shoulders.

 

Everyone except for two people.

 

Uh oh.

 

Agatha was leaned in, clearly whispering something into Rio’s ear. Her brown eyes were on the table, but her mouth had started to curl like she was about to laugh.

 

Agatha stared at the picture.

 

Yeah. Well. That might be a little damning.

 

The second picture was objectively worse.

 

Agatha was smirking straight into the camera. Both hands were resting lightly on Rio’s shoulders. Her cape, sheer and glittering, was lifted and blocking most of their upper bodies.  Rio had her hood up, and through the shimmer of fabric, her arms were crossed tightly, as if she didn’t trust her hands and needed them tucked away to behave. She wasn’t looking at the camera.

 

Rio was looking at her.

 

It wasn’t neutral. It wasn’t friendly. It was that stupid, tiny smile- barely there, lips just beginning to curve, eyes soft lidded and steady. The expression on Rio’s face felt impossibly intimate, especially in a photo that wasn’t supposed to look like anything at all.

 

That smile didn’t belong in pictures. It was private. Something Agatha had only ever seen when they were alone, never offered to anyone else, never meant to be witnessed from the outside.

 

And she had always known it was hers. Not wished. Not hoped. Known.

 

To see it captured like this, visible, exposed, sent back to Agatha without context or warning, felt indecent- less like a memory and more like a secret someone else had gotten their hands on.

 

It was right after they’d come back inside from eating each other’s faces off.

 

Jen had drunkenly screamed at them for a photo while they were still riding the high of breaking a seventeen year losing streak. Rio pulled her hood up, maybe to hide her face, maybe just to retreat a little. Judging by the look she was caught wearing, it hadn’t fucking helped.

 

Agatha had left not long after. She didn’t trust herself to stay. Not with Rio looking at her like that. Not with the taste of her still everywhere.

 

And now, staring at the photo, she could still see it. The flush in Rio’s lips, the slight swelling, the unmistakable aftermath of something that didn’t belong to anyone else.

 

Her phone buzzed in her hands, and she flinched, only then realizing she had been zoomed in on Rio’s mouth.

 

And for one deeply humiliating second, Agatha actually thanked her ex-wife for interrupting what had clearly been a very normal, very casual moment of hyper focusing on her best friend’s lips.

 

Then she read Wanda’s text.

 

Wanda M.: Didn’t realize you were still feeding strays…

 

Agatha let out a furious, disbelieving, “Oooooh,” as her thumbs flew across the screen, hammering out a response with enough force to threaten the lifespan of her purple iPhone’s screen protector.

 

Agatha: Projection’s a hell of a thing, Wanda. 

Agatha: There’s only one stray clawing at my door these days, and she doesn’t know when to fucking quit.

Agatha: I’ll spare you the suspense. It’s you! 

Agatha: xoxo 

Agatha: … bitch!

 

Agatha immediately texted Jen: Block her. Then she opened her dusty, barely used Facebook and blocked Wanda. 

 

Agatha slapped her phone face down on the coffee table and stormed off to get ready for work, muttering the whole way about how her rot time had been ruined. 

 

Which, to be fair, she hadn’t had much rot time left. Twelve minutes, give or take- but now the vibes were contaminated, and there was no salvaging them. The air felt different. Her couch felt different. Everything was tainted, and she blamed Wanda completely.

Agatha was charting. Jen, who had claimed one of the parent recliners behind her, had a juice box she’d stolen from the nutrition room and was sipping it obnoxiously loud while watching Agatha with the blank eyed intensity of a cat about to knock something off a shelf.

 

“Your posture is terrible,” Jen said between slurps. 

 

Agatha didn’t respond. Just kept typing, jaw tight, chart half finished and mind ten miles elsewhere.

 

It was creeping up on 4am, x-ray had already come and gone, and to Agatha’s inexplicable disappointment, it had been Teen assigned to the NICU that night.

 

“So you were talking about Wanda, right?” Jen asked.

 

Agatha paused mid charting, turned halfway in her seat. “What?”

 

“That text you sent me earlier. All it said was ‘block her.’ I assumed you meant Wanda?”

 

Agatha stared. Blinked. Then delivered the flattest, driest look she could possibly summon. 

 

“Obviously.”

 

Jen raised a brow. “I don’t know. You could’ve been talking about Ri-”

 

“I wasn’t.”

 

There wasn’t even a beat between the suggestion and Agatha shutting it down.

 

Jen sat up a little straighter. “Did something happen between you two?”

 

Agatha sputtered. Actually sputtered. “Wh-” She coughed once, tried to mask it as a casual laugh, and failed so fucking miserably. “No. Why-” Another shaky little noise that came out deeply guilty sounding. “Why would you even ask that?”

 

And then Agatha’s voice flattened, “Did she say something to you?”

 

Jen narrowed her eyes. “Okay. Yeah. You’re going to give me every single detail.”

 

“There are no details.”

 

“Liar.”

 

“I pierced her ears.”

 

“And?”

 

“That’s it.”

 

“Liar.”

 

“I’m not-”

 

“Yes you are.”

 

“I’m really not-”

 

“Agatha.”

 

Agatha exhaled sharply through her nose and hissed out, between clenched jaw, “Fine. We fucking kissed.”

 

Jen sat up like someone had dumped ice water down her shirt. “Oh my god.”

 

Agatha didn’t look at her.

 

Jen said it again, louder, “Oh my god, Agatha. That’s great!”

 

Oh, great. That tone. Like it was cute. Like it hadn’t detonated seventeen years of carefully compartmentalized bullshit in one stupid kiss.

 

Jen immediately backtracked. “That is great... isn’t it? Wait. Did it suck?”

 

“No.” Agatha whispered.

 

“What?”

 

“It did not suck,” she said through clenched teeth. “Quite the fucking opposite.”

 

Jen’s jaw dropped slightly.

 

“And that’s the fucking problem, Jennifer.”

 

“Why?”

 

Agatha could’ve said a hundred things- biting, sarcastic, safe. But none of them felt right. Or true. So she gave the smallest shrug she could manage without looking like she cared.

 

“I don’t know.”

 

“You still in denial?”

 

And what a fucking loaded question- and not for the first time.



Agatha couldn’t afford to say it out loud. It was too new. Too uncertain. Saying anything now might turn it into something it wasn’t ready to be. Something Agatha wasn't ready for it to be. 

 

“I’m in denial about a lot of things,” Agatha said quietly.

 

It was the closest thing to the truth she could give… again. 

 

Jen didn’t say anything right away. Agatha could hear the faint rustle of her shifting in the recliner, the subtle squeak of vinyl as she sat up a little straighter.

 

“Agatha… you’ve been in lo-“

 

Agatha swiveled her chair back around and tried to focus on the chart in front of her. “Don’t get sappy on me now, Jen.”

 

And Jen, to her credit, didn’t say anything else. Just took another long, obnoxious sip of juice and let Agatha pretend her hands weren’t shaking.

 

Some things weren’t ready for daylight. Not yet.

 

But that didn’t mean they wouldn’t grow.

Rio met her outside the NICU Saturday morning after shift change with a bottle of Diet Coke in hand. Agatha’s shift had been shit- her ex-wife had set the tone for it early, and it never really recovered. And the absence of Rio, even if it wasn’t supposed to matter, had only made it worse. But there she was. Asking how the night went. Offering to scold whichever baby had been causing Agatha trouble. Agatha laughed. She didn’t say what really made the shift unbearable. Didn’t say she’d wanted to see her.

 

Rio walked her all the way to her car. Told her she’d see her in twelve hours. Agatha groaned and told her not to remind her.

 

Agatha went home. Slept. Came back.

 

That night, she texted Rio - Break in 20 - and didn’t really think about what she expected. Rio was already waiting outside when she got there. They shared a cigarette and talked about a trauma case- motorcycle, crushed leg, Rio describing the way the bones moved when she lifted it. Agatha nearly gagged. Rio looked smug about it. 

 

The next morning, Rio walked her to her car again.

 

On Sunday, she came up to x-ray the babies. Caught Agatha’s eye more than once, and didn’t bother pretending not to. At some point, when things slowed down in the department, Rio came back -not with a machine, just herself- and dropped into one of the parent recliners at Agatha’s bedspace. Said they weren’t busy, and she had time. Agatha didn’t mind. She charted, she worked, she answered when Rio said something. It wasn’t a big deal. But it was… nice. Welcomed, even.

 

Every time Agatha caught a glimpse of Rio’s freshly pierced ears, something in her chest pulled tight. Not because of the piercings themselves, but because she’d done them. Her hands. Her choice. Hers. It had been hers. Brief, and maybe a accident, but hers all the same. And now it was walking around the hospital like proof. Proof she’d let something happen. Proof she’d wanted to.

 

It was stupid. And fleeting. And completely impossible to ignore.

 

Agatha didn’t let herself think about it too hard. She just wanted to be around Rio without turning it into anything.

 

None of it was a big deal.

 

Not really.

Agatha’s alarm went off at noon on Monday. She groaned and thrashed in bed, caught somewhere between exhaustion and rage. Her body ached from the weekend -three brutal night shifts back to back- and the nap she'd taken after getting home hadn’t come close to fixing it.

 

She trudged downstairs, whining with every step. She made her coffee in silence, barely awake enough to press the right buttons.

 

Then she collapsed onto the couch, remote already in hand, and turned on a Real Housewives franchise at random. She didn’t bother checking which one. She let it play, loud enough to keep her from dozing off again. She knew if she slept any longer, she’d wake up feeling worse.

 

Agatha’s phone started ringing, and the sound of it was fucking unbearable. She felt it in her skull, in her teeth, behind her eyes- like it was drilling straight into her nervous system. She groaned and leaned forward, reaching for it where it buzzed across the coffee table.

 

“Please don’t be my ex-wife. Please don’t be my ex-wife. Please don’t be my ex-wife,” she muttered, dragging herself upright.

 

She flipped the phone over and to her surprise, it wasn’t Wanda. It was an incoming FaceTime call from Rio. 

 

Agatha answered and was immediately greeted by the top half of Rio’s face, her forehead far too close to the camera.



“What,” Agatha said, not bothering to sound polite.

 

“Do you wanna hang out with me today?” Rio asked, voice slow and syrupy with sleep. At the end of the sentence, she lifted her chin just enough to flash a tight, toothy smile before sinking back down, hiding everything below her eyes again.

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Depends. What were you thinking?”

 

“They just opened the pool at my apartment,” Rio said. “I want to rot in the sun while no one’s out there.” She blinked at the camera, then away. “Would you like to join me, goose?”

 

Agatha squinted. “Goose?”

 

Rio gave a tired hum. “Yeah. ‘Cause you’re grumpy.” She rubbed at her face like it would help her stay conscious. “Grumpy goose.” As if it was obvious.

 

Agatha grimaced.

 

Rio, whenever she was sleep deprived, had the unfortunate habit of being impossibly… endearing. She always used to get quiet and mumbly and strangely sweet.

 

Agatha, on the other hand, fully accepted her role as the most irritable bird in the flock.

 

Agatha sighed. “What time?”

 

Not because she couldn’t be alone. She loved being alone. Thrived in it. She was simply… outsourcing her rot today. That was allowed.

 

“Whenever,” Rio murmured.

 

“How far are you from me?”

 

“Thirteen minutes.”

 

“Send me the address. I’ll be there in twenty five.”

 

“Yay,” Rio said, without an ounce of enthusiasm, and Agatha understood perfectly.

 

They were both too tired to fake it. That was the whole point. Post night shift, nothing felt real anyway. Words came out slower. Time got weird. Agatha didn’t need conversation or plans or anything that resembled effort. Just someone else who knew what it meant to still hear monitor beeps in your head hours after clocking out. Someone who wouldn’t flinch if she went completely still and stared at the sky like it held answers. 

 

Agatha could pretend that wasn’t what she needed. She’d done worse.

Agatha dug her swimsuit out from the back of her closet, buried beneath a stack of clothes she hadn’t touched since she moved back. A purple bikini. She held it up, gave it a quick once over, then stripped down and pulled it on.

 

She looked at herself in her bathroom mirror.

 

Yeah. She looked fucking hot.

 

Not in the wishful way. Not in the maybe if she tilts her head and squints way. It was fact. Her skin was soft and flushed from the shower. She looked alive. Solid. And just vain enough to know she didn’t need anyone else to confirm it.

 

Agatha applied her sunscreen alone in the bathroom, careful to get her shoulders and back. She absolutely could have asked Rio to do it for her. She absolutely wanted to. But she wasn’t going to hand herself over that easily. Not today.

 

They were friends.

 

Her eyes flicked to the sticky note still stuck to the corner of her mirror. Agatha closed them for a second and repeated it to herself like a mantra.

 

Agatha needed the lie to stay true a little longer. Just until she figured out what the hell she was doing.

 

She packed fast. Towel, sunscreen, change of clothes, hair tie, water bottle. Threw it all in a canvas tote. Then she pulled on an old oversized t-shirt, slid on her sandals, and headed out.

 

The drive to Rio’s was short. But the second she pulled up to the building, she clocked the difference. This place was far nicer than the last one Rio lived in. Gated, clean, almost too polished. She pulled up to the callbox, punched in the four digit code, hit the star key. The gate buzzed and swung open.

 

Inside, she found Rio’s building, parked in the guest lot, and shot off a quick H urry up text to Rio.

 

Rio appeared a few minutes later, and Agatha stepped out of the car to meet her, bag over her shoulder.

 

She looked exactly how Agatha expected her to- oversized t-shirt, sunglasses halfway down her nose, flip flops barely making a sound. A towel was draped over one arm, a small cooler slung across her shoulder with a faded rainbow strap, and a travel cup in her free hand.

 

Rio looked good.

 

Annoyingly good.

 

Not that it mattered. Agatha barely noticed. Didn’t care. She barely even fucking looked.

 

And if Agatha’s fingers twitched with the urge to fix her sunglasses, that was no one’s business but hers.

 

Agatha grunted a greeting. 

 

Rio, without saying anything, handed over the cup.

 

“What is it?” Agatha asked, taking it without hesitation, falling into step beside her.

 

“Espresso. Promise it’s stronger than whatever you make with that Keurig.”

 

Agatha took a sip. She paused.

 

“Holy shit. That’s good.”

 

Rio nodded. “It should be. That machine is the most expensive thing in my kitchen.”

 

Agatha didn’t respond.

 

The walk to the pool was quiet. Neither of them had the energy to fake being awake. Their steps dragged. Their brains were still loading.

 

Agatha felt just the edge of Rio’s hand brushing against hers. She glanced sideways. Rio was biting the inside of her lip, eyes ahead, brows drawn like she was deep in thought or trying not to be. Agatha told herself it was accidental.

 

Then it happened again. Slower this time. More intentional.

 

Agatha turned her head the other way, pretending to look at nothing, and let her finger skim the back of Rio’s hand. 

 

It didn’t count if she didn’t look.

 

By the time either of them might’ve said or done something, they were already at the gate.

 

The pool was nicer than Agatha expected. Sleek, bright, unnervingly pristine. A wide, shallow step spanned the far end, deep enough to let water glide over the tiles and lap at the bases of loungers that were built in. Beyond that, the pool slipped into a deeper blue. Still. Clear. Not a single ripple. No movement, no voices, no sound except for the distant hum of the heat and the faint scuff of their footsteps.

 

It was completely empty.

 

Thank fuck.

 

Agatha claimed a table under an umbrella and dropped her bag onto it. Rio did the same- but in one blink, her t-shirt and flip flops were gone, peeled off and discarded in one smooth motion, and she was already walking toward the loungers, bare shoulders catching the sun, tan skin golden and glowing and absolutely not giving Agatha a second to prepare.

 

Agatha scoffed under her breath. Rude. Honestly rude. She didn’t even get the satisfaction of watching her undress- didn’t get a single gratuitous second to linger, to drag her eyes up inch by slow inch of newly exposed- 

 

Agatha let her gaze drop anyway, and all that annoyance vanished.

 

The black bikini Rio wore was almost laughably minimal- nothing but thin straps up top and, below, a thong bottom that did absolutely nothing to protect Agatha’s sanity. The fabric curved high on Rio’s hips and disappeared entirely in the back, leaving the full view of her ass on unapologetic display. There was no room for modesty. No room for Agatha to look without consequences.

 

Agatha’s tongue pressed into the inside of her cheek. Her eyes stayed locked on Rio’s ass, helpless. Her hands twitched at her sides. Desperate to follow.

 

She didn’t move, but the pull was visceral, dragging her forward in spirit if not in flesh- like a lamb to slaughter, holy and doomed, too far gone to pretend she wouldn’t kneel.

 

A tiny, unbidden whimper clawed its way out of Agatha’s throat before she could stop it.

 

This was fine. Normal. Agatha could exist in the same zip code as that ass without losing her grip on reality. She could be cool. Casual. Normal.

 

Agatha should really look away. 

 

She didn’t. 

 

She needed a minute. Maybe several.

 

Rio finally settled into one of the loungers, legs stretched out and Agatha had never been more jealous of a goddamn piece of furniture in her life.

 

Agatha didn’t look. Not at first. She busied herself with nothing- adjusting her sunglasses, smoothing the hem of her shirt, pretending the view didn’t exist.

 

But she could feel it. She always could.

 

Agatha kept her eyes low as long as she could, but the weight of it pressed against her until she caved and glanced up- 

 

Rio was already looking at her.

 

Sunglasses slid halfway down her nose, brows arched just enough to ask a question she had no intention of saying out loud. Her mouth twitched, not quite a smirk. Relaxed. Confident.

 

Oh fuuuuuuuck.

 

Agatha could’ve ignored it. Looked away. Played dumb.

 

She didn’t.

 

Instead, she reached for the hem of her shirt and started to peel it off, slow and methodical. Not for effect. Not to flirt. Just to prove she could. The fabric clung to her for half a second before giving way, sliding over her ribs, her chest, her shoulders.

 

By the time the shirt cleared her head, Rio’s gaze was glued to her chest.

 

Agatha’s breath caught.

 

Then Rio licked her lips.

 

It wasn’t purposeful. It wasn’t a move. Just instinct. A flash of tongue, barely there, quick and unconscious and somehow worse because of it. That single flash of tongue had Agatha’s brain shorting out entirely.

 

Agatha wanted to press her palms against untouched skin that had haunted her for years. To stake some long overdue claim on what always should’ve belonged to her. To make sure no one else ever- 

 

Get a grip. Get a fucking grip.

 

She dragged her gaze away from Rio and started toward the lounger beside her, trying not to trip over every thought currently screaming inside her head.

 

Agatha dropped into the lounger with a dramatic grunt, limbs sprawled,  surrendering to the sun instead of the situation.

 

“You good?” Rio asked.

 

“Yep,” Agatha said, eyes pinned to the sky.

 

Agatha could feel Rio’s brown eyes boring holes into the side of her skull. The full turn of her head, the deliberate silence- it was all so pointed it might as well have been spoken. Agatha could practically hear the smirk forming. Tongue against cheek. That stupid fucking tell Rio had never grown out of.

 

“I didn’t see you put on sunscreen.”

 

Here we go.

Of course that was the first thing out of Rio Vidal’s fucking mouth.

 

Agatha had put it on at home -alone, in the bathroom, twisting to reach her back like an idiot- because it had felt like the smart thing to do. Her brain had made that call hours ago- before Rio’s face, her voice, and her insane ass had entered the equation. Now she was sitting here, half naked, bathed in sunlight and suddenly regretting every responsible decision she'd made before walking out the door.

 

She didn’t glance over. Just let the silence hang between them- almost daring Rio to fill it.

 

Let her look, Agatha’s brain whispered. 

 

Agatha slid deeper into the lounger, arms stretching overhead, spine arching just slightly as she adjusted her weight. One leg bent at the knee, casual. Thoughtless. A move meant to get comfortable, except she knew exactly what it looked like.

 

Just enough to make Agatha feel a little less stupid for doing everything right and still wanting to be touched.

Agatha heard the soft shuffle of her feet retreating, the creak of a drawer opening, the quiet hush of movement as Rio crossed her own bedroom. A moment later, her footsteps padded down the hall toward the guest bathroom. 

 

Agatha stood there for another second, alone with the echo of a scratched record and her own heartbeat.

Showering at Rio’s was a terrible idea.

 

Eucalyptus hung in a bunch from the shower head, slightly browned at the edges, still fragrant in the steam. Agatha tried not to stare at it. 

 

She stood under the water, chest turned to the spray, hair still dry- no point washing it. She hadn’t gone under water in the pool- at least not physically. That, and she couldn’t stomach the idea of using Rio’s shampoo.

 

The soap had been a reflex. Agatha didn’t think about it until the scent hit her- too clean, too sweet, familiar in a way that scraped at her ribs. It clung to her, buried itself in her skin, and the towel only made it worse. 

 

Agatha had grabbed the first one she saw, thick and worn from use. The fabric reeked of Rio’s detergent, warm and chemical and so distinctly hers that Agatha nearly gagged on it. She tried not to think about how often Rio had used this exact towel, how many times she’d wrapped it around herself with dripping hair and bare shoulders. It was inescapable. Even after she got dressed, her own clothes couldn’t smother it. She still smelled like Rio. It had worked itself into every seam.

 

They ended up on the couch, neither of them saying much. They sat close, but not touching, a careful few inches of space between them.

 

Agatha had picked the movie- Little Shop of Horrors . She told herself it was because it was there, because it was safe, because she hadn’t thought it through until it was too late. Halfway in, she regretted it entirely.

 

Rio used to play it on a loop until Agatha knew every line by heart. And now, with it playing softly in front of them, she wanted to vomit.



Not at the movie itself, but at the mushiness of it all. The softness. The stupid, sentimental instinct that made Agatha put it on in the first place. She could hear Rio mouthing along to “Skid Row (Downtown)” beside her without even thinking and it made her stomach turn.

 

Agatha hadn’t picked it to be kind. Or maybe she had. She definitely had. And that was the problem. It was so unlike her. Or maybe it wasn’t, maybe it was exactly like her. Maybe that’s why she hated it.

She kept her eyes on the screen, jaw tight, fists curled in her lap like she could wring the weakness out of her palms. Still taking up space like she always had- quietly, relentlessly, without asking.

Like it wasn’t, in some fucked up way, a love letter.

 

“I’m gonna ask you this,” Rio said finally, still looking at her phone. “And I fucking hope your answer’s changed in the last decade… What pizza do you like?”

Said she couldn’t stomach the idea of her own slice so much as brushing against the sludge Agatha ordered. They used to get two different pizza’s just to keep the peace, and even then, Rio would make a show of sealing Agatha's box closed like it was a biohazard.

Rio recoiled like she’d been physically slapped. “No. No, no, no. Agatha. Pineapple? You’re still- Jesus. You’re still doing this?”

 

“It’s good,” Agatha said, smug now. “It’s sweet and salty. It’s balanced. Like… culinarily. It’s science.”

 

“It’s fruit on cheese. That’s not science, that’s a hate crime.”

 

“Tomatoes are fruit. Pizza sauce is fruit. You're already eating fruit, asshole.”

Agatha snorted. “You just don’t like it because you’re a coward. You fear flavor.”

 

“I fear soggy crust and betrayal. Pineapple leaks juice, Agatha. It leaks. It seeps into everything. I used to taste the betrayal on my half when you ordered that garbage.”

 

“That’s why we got separate pizzas every time.”

 

Rio nodded. “Because I don’t believe in cross contamination.”

 

“You’re so dramatic,” Agatha muttered.

 

Rio glanced at her, unimpressed. “I’ve had pineapple flavored crust trauma. I’m allowed to be dramatic.”

 

Rio was still fiddling with the order, tapping her thumb against the phone screen like she was pretending this didn’t feel familiar. Like they hadn’t done this exact dance a dozen times before.

 

“Same place?” Agatha asked.

 

“Obviously.” Rio tossed her phone onto the cushion between them and leaned back, arms crossed. “Forty minutes.”

 

Agatha nodded.

 

They both looked at the screen again. The movie was still going- bright and absurd, soaked in sentiment.

When they were done eating, neither of them moved. Agatha grabbed the quilt from the back of the couch and threw it over both their legs without comment. They still weren’t touching, not exactly, but they were close enough that it wouldn’t have taken much. Close enough that her bare knee kept brushing against Rio’s thigh whenever she adjusted. Bulb lights were strung overhead, screwed into the siding and the overhang, uneven and slightly drooping between bolts. One flickered every few seconds like it couldn’t make up its mind.

 

There was only one hanging plant, a long, leafy thing by the sliding door that swayed in the breeze.  The rest were arranged along a simple wooden bench on the far end, nestled in mismatched pots- ceramic, clay, chipped enamel.

She had a cigarette in one hand, smoke curling past her lips as she talked about how her old shithole apartment had somehow paid off. How she’d saved and waited and waited some more. How this place was finally hers. She liked it.

Rio nodded like she was answering the question, even if she wasn’t. She took one last drag from her cigarette and hummed around it, then leaned past Agatha to stub it out. Her hands came to rest on the railing, one on each side of Agatha’s body, and she stepped in. Closer. A few inches between them now. Not even that. She blew the smoke to the side, her voice low. “So many, Agatha. I was fighting women off all night. It was vicious. Bloody.”

 

Agatha fake pouted, lips curved. “Poor baby.” Her fingers moved along the seam of Rio’s shoulder lazily.

 

“Yeah. Poor me.” Rio’s voice dropped a little, teasing. “I was promised backup, and someone bailed.”

 

“I was working,” Agatha said, amused. “Keeping babies from trying to crawl toward the light.”

 

“Mm.” Rio squinted like she was pretending to weigh that. “Valid. But I’ll have you know it got dicey out there. I almost died.”

 

 “Eh. You survived.” Agatha shrugged.

 

“By the skin of my teeth.” Rio grinned and snapped her teeth in Agatha’s direction like she might actually bite her.

 

The gap between Rio's teeth had never once stopped being endearing, not even when Agatha tried to pretend it had.

 

Agatha snuffed her cigarette in the tray beside her and shook her head. “Weirdo.” She was still smiling, cheeks aching from it.

 

“I don’t see you complaining,” Rio said, nodding between their bodies like their closeness was all the proof she needed.

 

Agatha didn’t respond. Instead, she let her hand drift from Rio’s shoulder, fingers trailing up to the back of her neck.  She didn’t think about whether it was a good idea. She didn’t calculate the fallout. She just did what she wanted to do. For once. Without justifying it.

 

Agatha leaned in and kissed her.

 

Their mouths met gently, and Agatha held there- without urgency, without force. Just the soft, certain press of her lips to Rio’s.

 

Rio didn’t flinch or fall back. She breathed out against Agatha’s mouth and kissed her again. This time longer. This time with more certainty.

 

Then again.

 

And again.

 

Each one a little fuller than the last. Each one asking a question and receiving the same answer.

 

Agatha let it happen. Let herself want it. She didn’t rush or overthink it, didn’t try to force meaning onto the moment, but she felt the way her body stilled into it. The way her hands softened where they touched Rio. The way the air around them seemed to narrow until all she could feel was Rio’s breath, her mouth, the way she kept coming back like it was the most natural thing in the world.

 

When Agatha finally pulled back, she didn’t go far. Her hands found their way to Rio’s waist, resting there for a beat before curling under the hem of her hoodie. She glanced down at the space between them and how little of it there was. The fabric gave easily, and her palms slipped beneath, coming to rest against Rio’s bare back.

 

Rio exhaled when Agatha touched her like that- fully, soundlessly. When Agatha pulled her in, arms wrapped around her like she had every right. Rio went without resistance.

 

Agatha let herself explore. Her fingers traced the familiar shape of Rio’s spine, nails lightly dragging as if to mark her place. She didn’t know why she was doing it except that she could. Rio’s arms closed around Agatha’s shoulders like a sigh. Agatha felt the brush of lips against her hair.

 

Agatha closed her eyes. She had to. Everything in her felt like it was turning inside out. The closeness. The stillness. The goddamn kindness of it. Not just now, but all day. Every stupid softness she'd let herself accept. She breathed out shakily, trying to reel herself in. Her voice, when it came, barely cleared her throat. “I should probably go home.”

 

Rio didn’t move at first. Then she shifted back just enough to meet Agatha eyes. “I want you to stay,” Rio said softly.

 

Agatha’s eyes slammed shut this time, too fast, trying to block out the words by refusing to look at them.

 

Once, she would’ve done anything to hear that. Would’ve set the world on fire to be wanted like that. And now here it was, handed to her plain and unadorned.

 

And she couldn’t even look at Rio.

 

Rio must have seen it- the way Agatha’s body stilled, the way her hands gripped tighter like she was bracing for the impact of something unspoken. She pulled back even more, softening her tone like she could smooth it over.

 

“Just to hang out,” Rio added quickly, eyes flicking down and then back. “That’s all. If you want.” A pause. Then quieter: “You should stay.”

 

“Okay,” Agatha whispered. 

 

That would’ve always been the answer. No matter the time. No matter the cost. If Rio ever asked, the answer would always be yes. It had never been anything else.

 

But still, Agatha played at indifference. Still, she pretended her heart hadn’t just fallen out of her mouth and landed -whole and stupidly willing- in the hands of the one person she’d never been able to take it back from.
